color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">1,348.1\n</td></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: MetOffice<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n<p>date=July 2013\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Glasgow" title="Demography of Glasgow">Demography of Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Glasgow#Demographics" title="Geography of Glasgow">Geography of Glasgow \xc2\xa7&#160;Demographics</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_effect" title="Glasgow effect">Glasgow effect</a></div>\n<p>In the 1950s, the population of the City of Glasgow area peaked at 1,089,000. Glasgow was then one of the most densely populated cities in the world. After the 1960s, clearances of poverty-stricken inner city areas like the <a href="/wiki/Gorbals" title="Gorbals">Gorbals</a> and relocation to "<a href="/wiki/New_town#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="New town">new towns</a>" such as <a href="/wiki/East_Kilbride" title="East Kilbride">East Kilbride</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cumbernauld" title="Cumbernauld">Cumbernauld</a> led to population decline. In addition, the boundaries of the city were changed twice during the late-twentieth century, making direct comparisons difficult. The city continues to expand beyond the city council boundaries into surrounding suburban areas, encompassing around 400 square miles (1,040&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of all adjoining suburbs, if <a href="/wiki/Commuter_town" title="Commuter town">commuter towns</a> and villages are included. There are two distinct definitions for the population of Glasgow: the <b>Glasgow City Council Area</b> (which lost the districts of <a href="/wiki/Rutherglen" title="Rutherglen">Rutherglen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambuslang" title="Cambuslang">Cambuslang</a> to <a href="/wiki/South_Lanarkshire" title="South Lanarkshire">South Lanarkshire</a> in 1996) and the <b><a href="/wiki/Greater_Glasgow" title="Greater Glasgow">Greater Glasgow</a> Urban Area</b> (which includes the conurbation around the city).\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Location\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th>Area\n</th>\n<th>Density\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Glasgow City Council</b><sup id="cite_ref-gro_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gro-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>592,820\n</td>\n<td>67.76&#160;sq&#160;mi (175.5&#160;km<sup>2</sup>)\n</td>\n<td>8,541.8/sq&#160;mi (3,298.0/km<sup>2</sup>)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Greater Glasgow Urban Area</b><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>1,199,629\n</td>\n<td>142.27&#160;sq&#160;mi (368.5&#160;km<sup>2</sup>)\n</td>\n<td>8,212.9/sq&#160;mi (3,171.0/km<sup>2</sup>)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="5" style="text-align: center;"><small><b>Source:</b> <i>Scotland\'s Census Results Online</i><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Glasgow\'s population influx in the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries was related to economic expansion as well as internally generated growth with the vast majority of newcomers to the city from outside Scotland being from <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, especially the north western counties of <a href="/wiki/County_Donegal" title="County Donegal">Donegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Fermanagh" title="County Fermanagh">Fermanagh</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Tyrone" title="County Tyrone">Tyrone</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Londonderry" title="County Londonderry">Derry</a>. In the 1881 UK Census, 83% of the population was born in Scotland, 13% in Ireland, 3% in England and 1% elsewhere. By 1911, the city was no longer gaining population by migration. The demographic percentages in the 1951 UK census were: born in Scotland 93%, Ireland 3%, England 3% and elsewhere 1%.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In the early-twentieth century, many <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanian</a> refugees began to settle in Glasgow and at its height in the 1950s; there were around 10,000 in the Glasgow area.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/Italian_Scots" title="Italian Scots">Italian Scots</a> also settled in Glasgow, originating from provinces like <a href="/wiki/Frosinone" title="Frosinone">Frosinone</a> between <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucca" title="Lucca">Lucca</a> in north-west <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a> at this time, many originally working as "<a href="/wiki/Hokey_pokey_(ice_cream)" title="Hokey pokey (ice cream)">Hokey Pokey</a>" men.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center><b>Historical population and city limits</b></center>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; border: none;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th data-sort-type="year">Year<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th>Area <br /> (km\xc2\xb2)\n</th>\n<th>Density <br /> (inh./km\xc2\xb2)\n</th>\n<th>Area changes\n</th></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1300</td>\n<td>1,500</td>\n<td>-<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>Initial\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1600</td>\n<td>7,000</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td>Unknown\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1791</td>\n<td>66,000</td>\n<td>7.16</td>\n<td>9,217</td>\n<td>Anderson to James Street/West Nile Street to Camlachie\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1831</td>\n<td>202,426</td>\n<td>8.83</td>\n<td>22,924</td>\n<td>Necropolis and Blythswood\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1846</td>\n<td>280,000</td>\n<td>23.44</td>\n<td>11,945</td>\n<td>Burghs of Anderston and Calton/Barony of Gorbals\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1872</td>\n<td>494,824</td>\n<td>24.42</td>\n<td>20,263</td>\n<td>Districts of Keppochhill, Alexandra Parade and the new Glasgow University grounds\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1891</td>\n<td>658,073</td>\n<td>48.00</td>\n<td>13,709</td>\n<td>Burghs of Govanhill, Crosshill, Pollokshields, Maryhill and Hillhead. Districts of Blackhill, Shawfield and the east end of Glasgow Green\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1912</td>\n<td>800,000</td>\n<td>77.63</td>\n<td>10,305</td>\n<td>Burghs of Govan, Partick, Pollokshaws. Districts of Shettleston, Tollcross, West of Govan, Cathcart, <br /> Newlands, West of Partick, Dawsholm, Temple and Knightswood.\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1921</td>\n<td>1,034,174</td>\n<td>77.63</td>\n<td>13,321</td>\n<td>No change\n</td></tr>\n<tr Nitshill, Hurlet, Crookston, Cardonald, Scotstoun, Yoker and Knightswood.\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1938</td>\n<td>1,127,825</td>\n<td>160.77</td>\n<td>7,015</td>\n<td>Districts of Balmuildy, Auchinairn, Cardowan, Gartloch, Queenslie, Linn Park, Jenny Lind, Easterhouse, <br /> Darnley, Penilee, Drumry, Drumchapel, Summerston, Hogganfield and Carntyne\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1981</td>\n<td>774,068</td>\n<td>202.35</td>\n<td>3,825</td>\n<td>Burghs of Rutherglen, Cambuslang, Mount Vernon, Baillieston.\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>1991</td>\n<td>688,600</td>\n<td>202.67</td>\n<td>3,397</td>\n<td>Minor boundary change\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>2001</td>\n<td>586,710</td>\n<td>177.30</td>\n<td>3,309</td>\n<td>Rutherglen and Cambuslang transferred to South Lanarkshire.\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>2011</td>\n<td>599,650</td>\n<td>174.70</td>\n<td>3,432</td>\n<td>Minor boundary change\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In the 1960s and 1970s, many <a href="/wiki/Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="Asians">Asians</a> also settled in Glasgow, mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Pollokshields" title="Pollokshields">Pollokshields</a> area. These number 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani people">Pakistanis</a>, 15,000 <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a> and 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladeshi people">Bangladeshis</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_people" title="Cantonese people">Chinese</a> people, many of whom settled in the <a href="/wiki/Garnethill" title="Garnethill">Garnethill</a> area of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Since 2000, the UK government has pursued a policy of dispersal of <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_Kingdom_since_1922" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration to the United Kingdom since 1922">asylum seekers</a> to ease pressure on social housing in the <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> area. The city is also home to some 8,406 (1.42%) <a href="/wiki/Polish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish people">Polish people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-crer_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crer-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" id="toc" style="float:right; margin-left:2em; width:40%; font-size:85%;" cellspacing="3">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4"><b>Glasgow compared</b><sup id="cite_ref-crer_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crer-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-glasgow.gov.uk_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glasgow.gov.uk-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">UK Census 2011</a></b></td>\n<td><b>Glasgow</b></td>\n<td><b>Scotland</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Total population</td>\n<td>599,650</td>\n<td>5,295,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Population growth 2001\xe2\x80\x932011</td>\n<td>2.7%</td>\n<td>5.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>White</td>\n<td>88.4%</td>\n<td>96.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Asian</td>\n<td>8.1%</td>\n<td>2.7%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Black</td>\n<td>2.4%</td>\n<td>0.8%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Christian</td>\n<td>54.5%</td>\n<td>54.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Muslim</td>\n<td>5.4%</td>\n<td>1.4%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">United Kingdom Census 2001</a> the population decline has been reversed. The population was static for a time; but due to migration from other parts of Scotland as well as immigration from overseas, the population has begun to grow. The population of the city council area was 593,245 in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and around 2,300,000 people live in the Glasgow <a href="/wiki/Travel_to_work_area" title="Travel to work area">travel to work area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spt_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spt-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> This area is defined as consisting of over 10% of residents travelling into Glasgow to work and is without fixed boundaries.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The population density of London following the 2011 census was recorded as 5,200 people per square kilometre, while 3,395 people per square kilometre were registered in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-Dense_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dense-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In 1931, the population density was 16,166/sq&#160;mi (6,242/km<sup>2</sup>), highlighting the "clearances" into the suburbs and new towns that were built to reduce the size of one of Europe\'s most densely populated cities.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005, Glasgow had the lowest <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of any UK city at 72.9 years.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Much was made of this during the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_East_by-election,_2008" title="Glasgow East by-election, 2008">2008 Glasgow East by-election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, a <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> report about health inequalities, revealing that male life expectancy varied from 54 years in <a href="/wiki/Calton,_Glasgow" title="Calton, Glasgow">Calton</a> to 82 years in nearby <a href="/wiki/Lenzie" title="Lenzie">Lenzie</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Dunbartonshire" title="East Dunbartonshire">East Dunbartonshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Areas_and_suburbs">Areas and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Areas and suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgowareas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Glasgowareas.jpg/250px-Glasgowareas.jpg" width="250" height="193" class="thumbimage" 2x" data-file-width="1492" data-file-height="1151" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgowareas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Areas_of_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="Areas of Glasgow">Areas of Glasgow</a>. Click to enlarge.</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_centre">City centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: City centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_city_centre" title="Glasgow city centre">city centre</a> is bounded by the High Street to the east, the River Clyde to the south and the <a href="/wiki/M8_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M8 motorway (Scotland)">M8 motorway</a> to the west and north, which was built through the <a href="/wiki/Townhead" title="Townhead">Townhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross,_Glasgow" title="Charing Cross, Glasgow">Charing Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cowcaddens" title="Cowcaddens">Cowcaddens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anderston" title="Anderston">Anderston</a> areas in the 1960s.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail_and_theatre_district">Retail and theatre district</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Retail and theatre district">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:(looking_down)_Buchanan_Street,_Glasgow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking down <a href="/wiki/Buchanan_Street" title="Buchanan Street">Buchanan Street</a> towards <a href="/wiki/St_Enoch_subway_station" title="St Enoch subway station">St Enoch subway station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The city centre is based on a <a href="/wiki/Grid_plan" title="Grid plan">grid system</a> of streets on the north bank of the River Clyde. The heart of the city is <a href="/wiki/George_Square" title="George Square">George Square</a>, site of many of <a href="/wiki/Public_statues_in_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="Public statues in Glasgow">Glasgow\'s public statues</a> and the elaborate Victorian <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Chambers" title="Glasgow City Chambers">Glasgow City Chambers</a>, headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="Politics of Glasgow">Glasgow City Council</a>. To the south and west are the shopping precincts of <a href="/wiki/Argyle_Street,_Glasgow" title="Argyle Street, Glasgow">Argyle Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sauchiehall_Street" title="Sauchiehall Street">Sauchiehall Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buchanan_Street" title="Buchanan Street">Buchanan Street</a>, the last featuring more upmarket retailers and winner of the Academy of Urbanism "Great Street Award" 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The collection of shops around these streets accumulate to become known as "The Style Mile".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main shopping centres are Buchanan Galleries and the <a href="/wiki/St._Enoch_Centre" title="St. Enoch Centre">St. Enoch Centre</a> (located adjacent to <a href="/wiki/St_Enoch_Square" title="St Enoch Square">St Enoch Square</a>), with the up-market <a href="/wiki/Princes_Square" title="Princes Square">Princes Square</a>, which specifically features shops such as Ted Baker, Radley and Kurt Geiger.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The Italian Centre also specialises in designer labels. The London-based department store <a href="/wiki/Selfridges" title="Selfridges">Selfridges</a> purchased a site in the city some years ago as part of its plans to expand stores\xe2\x80\x94plans now shelved, according to the company. Glasgow\'s retail portfolio forms the UK\'s second largest and most economically important retail sector after Central London.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city centre is home to most of Glasgow\'s main cultural venues: the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Glasgow" title="Theatre Royal, Glasgow">Theatre Royal</a> (performing home of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Opera" title="Scottish Opera">Scottish Opera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Ballet" title="Scottish Ballet">Scottish Ballet</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Pavilion_Theatre_(Glasgow)" title="Pavilion Theatre (Glasgow)">Pavilion Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Theatre,_Glasgow" title="King&#39;s Theatre, Glasgow">King\'s Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Glasgow Royal Concert Hall">Glasgow Royal Concert Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Film_Theatre" title="Glasgow Film Theatre">Glasgow Film Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tron_Theatre" title="Tron Theatre">Tron Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallery_of_Modern_Art,_Glasgow" title="Gallery of Modern Art, Glasgow">Gallery of Modern Art</a> (GoMA), Mitchell Library and Theatre, the <a href="/wiki/CCA_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="CCA Glasgow">Centre for Contemporary Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/McLellan_Galleries" title="McLellan Galleries">McLellan Galleries</a> and the <a href="/wiki/The_Lighthouse_(Glasgow)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lighthouse (Glasgow)">Lighthouse Museum of Architecture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cineworld_(Glasgow)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cineworld (Glasgow)">The world\'s tallest cinema</a>, the eighteen-screen <a href="/wiki/Cineworld" title="Cineworld">Cineworld</a>, is situated on Renfrew Street. The city centre is also home to four of Glasgow\'s higher education institutions: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strathclyde" title="University of Strathclyde">University of Strathclyde</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Conservatoire_of_Scotland" title="Royal Conservatoire of Scotland">Royal Conservatoire of Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_School_of_Art" title="Glasgow School of Art">Glasgow School of Art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Caledonian_University" title="Glasgow Caledonian University">Glasgow Caledonian University</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchant_City">Merchant City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Merchant City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple,_Glasgow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple%2C_Glasgow.jpg/250px-Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple%2C_Glasgow.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple%2C_Glasgow.jpg/375px-Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple%2C_Glasgow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple%2C_Glasgow.jpg/500px-Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple%2C_Glasgow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Tolbooth_Steeple,_Glasgow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Tolbooth Steeple dominates <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cross" title="Glasgow Cross">Glasgow Cross</a> and marks the east side of the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_City" title="Merchant City">Merchant City</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>To the east is the commercial and residential district of <a href="/wiki/Merchant_City" title="Merchant City">Merchant City</a>. The Merchant City was formerly the residential district of the wealthy city merchants in the 18th and early 19th centuries, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Lords" title="Tobacco Lords">Tobacco Lords</a> from whom many of the streets take their name. As the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> and the wealth it brought to the city resulted in the expansion of Glasgow\'s central area westward, the original medieval centre was left behind. Glasgow Cross, situated at the junction of <a href="/wiki/High_Street_(Glasgow)" class="mw-redirect" title="High Street (Glasgow)">High Street</a>, Gallowgate, <a href="/wiki/Trongate" title="Trongate">Trongate</a> and Saltmarket was the original centre of the city, symbolised by its <a href="/wiki/Mercat_cross" title="Mercat cross">Mercat cross</a>. Glasgow Cross encompasses the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_City" title="Merchant City">Tolbooth</a> Clock Tower; all that remains of the original City Chambers, which was destroyed by fire in 1926. Moving northward up High Street towards <a href="/wiki/Rottenrow" title="Rottenrow">Rottenrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Townhead" title="Townhead">Townhead</a> lies the 15th century <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cathedral" title="Glasgow Cathedral">Glasgow Cathedral</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Provand%27s_Lordship" title="Provand&#39;s Lordship">Provand\'s Lordship</a>. Due to growing industrial pollution levels in the mid-to-late 19th century, the area fell out of favour with residents.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the late 1980s onwards, the Merchant City has been rejuvenated with luxury city centre flats and <a href="/wiki/Warehouse_conversion" class="mw-redirect" title="Warehouse conversion">warehouse conversions</a>. This regeneration has supported an increasing number of caf\xc3\xa9s and restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The area is also home to a number of high end boutique style shops and some of Glasgow\'s most upmarket stores.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Merchant City is the centre of Glasgow\'s growing "cultural quarter", based on King Street, the Saltmarket and <a href="/wiki/Trongate" title="Trongate">Trongate</a>, and at the heart of the annual <a href="/wiki/Merchant_City_Festival" title="Merchant City Festival">Merchant City Festival</a>. The area has supported a huge growth in art galleries, the origins of which can be found in the late 1980s when it attracted artist-led organisations that could afford the cheap rents required to operate in vacant manufacturing or retail spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The artistic and cultural potential of the Merchant City as a "cultural quarter" was harnessed by independent arts organisations and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Council" title="Glasgow City Council">Glasgow City Council</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and the recent development of Trongate 103, which houses galleries, workshops, artist studios and production spaces, is considered a major outcome of the continued partnership between both.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The area also contains a number of theatres and concert venues, including the <a href="/wiki/Tron_Theatre" title="Tron Theatre">Tron Theatre</a>, the Old Fruitmarket, the Trades Hall, St. Andrew\'s in the Square, Merchant Square, and the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow City Hall">City Halls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Financial_District_.28IFSD.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_District_(IFSD)">Financial District (IFSD)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Financial District (IFSD)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ClydeArc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/ClydeArc.jpg/250px-ClydeArc.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/ClydeArc.jpg/375px-ClydeArc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/ClydeArc.jpg/500px-ClydeArc.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ClydeArc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Clyde_Arc" title="Clyde Arc">Clyde Arc</a>, also known as "Squinty Bridge"</div></div></div>\n<p>To the western edge of the city centre, occupying the areas of <a href="/wiki/Blythswood_Hill" title="Blythswood Hill">Blythswood Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anderston" title="Anderston">Anderston</a>, lies Glasgow\'s financial district, known officially as the <a href="/wiki/International_Financial_Services_District" title="International Financial Services District">International Financial Services District</a> (IFSD), although often irreverently nicknamed by the contemporary press as the "square kilometre" or "Wall Street on Clyde".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Since the late 1980s the construction of many modern office blocks and high rise developments have paved the way for the IFSD to become one of the UK\'s largest financial quarters. With a reputation as an established financial services centre, coupled with comprehensive support services, Glasgow continues to attract and grow new business.\n</p><p>Of the 10 largest general insurance companies in the UK, 8 have a base or head office in Glasgow&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 including <a href="/wiki/Direct_Line" title="Direct Line">Direct Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esure" title="Esure">Esure</a>, <a href="/wiki/AXA" title="AXA">AXA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_Union" title="Norwich Union">Norwich Union</a>. Key banking sector companies have also moved some of their services to commercial property in Glasgow&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Resolution_plc" title="Resolution plc">Resolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Wealth" title="Barclays Wealth">Barclays Wealth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tesco_Personal_Finance" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesco Personal Finance">Tesco Personal Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lloyds_Banking_Group" title="Lloyds Banking Group">Lloyds Banking Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clydesdale_Bank" title="Clydesdale Bank">Clydesdale Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas" title="BNP Paribas">BNP Paribas</a>, <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander_UK" title="Santander UK">Santander</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland" title="Royal Bank of Scotland">Royal Bank of Scotland</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> have several departments and <a href="/wiki/Peel_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Peel Group">Clydeport</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Stock_Exchange" title="Glasgow Stock Exchange">Glasgow Stock Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Student_Loans_Company" title="Student Loans Company">Student Loans Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Executive_Enterprise,_Transport_and_Lifelong_Learning_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Executive Enterprise, Transport and Lifelong Learning Department">Scottish Executive Enterprise, Transport and Lifelong Learning Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Friendly" title="Scottish Friendly">Scottish Friendly</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Qualifications_Authority" title="Scottish Qualifications Authority">Scottish Qualifications Authority</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Enterprise" title="Scottish Enterprise">Scottish Enterprise</a> also have their headquarters in the district. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> also have one of their six worldwide Shared Business Centres located in the IFSD. <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Worldwide" title="Hilton Worldwide">Hilton</a> have a corporate office based in the area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_End">West End</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: West End">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG/250px-Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG/375px-Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG/500px-Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Side_View_of_the_Kelvingrove_Art_Museum.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Art_Gallery_and_Museum" title="Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum">Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum</a> is Glasgow\'s premier museum and art gallery, housing one of Europe\'s best civic art collections.</div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow\'s West End is a <a href="/wiki/Bohemianism" title="Bohemianism">bohemian</a> district of caf\xc3\xa9s, tea rooms, bars, boutiques, upmarket hotels, clubs and restaurants in the hinterland of <a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Park" title="Kelvingrove Park">Kelvingrove Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Botanic_Gardens" title="Glasgow Botanic Gardens">Glasgow Botanic Gardens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Exhibition_and_Conference_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre">Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre</a>, focused especially on the area\'s main thoroughfare, <a href="/wiki/Byres_Road" title="Byres Road">Byres Road</a>. The area is popular with tourists, and contains many hotels.\n</p><p>The West End includes residential areas of <a href="/wiki/Hillhead" title="Hillhead">Hillhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dowanhill" title="Dowanhill">Dowanhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Park" title="Kelvingrove Park">Kelvingrove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvinside" title="Kelvinside">Kelvinside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyndland" title="Hyndland">Hyndland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broomhill,_Glasgow" title="Broomhill, Glasgow">Broomhill</a>, and, to an increasing extent, <a href="/wiki/Partick" title="Partick">Partick</a>. The name is also increasingly being used to refer to any area to the west of <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross,_Glasgow" title="Charing Cross, Glasgow">Charing Cross</a>. This includes areas such as <a href="/wiki/Scotstoun" title="Scotstoun">Scotstoun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordanhill" title="Jordanhill">Jordanhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvindale" title="Kelvindale">Kelvindale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anniesland" title="Anniesland">Anniesland</a>.\n</p><p>The West End is bisected by the <a href="/wiki/River_Kelvin" title="River Kelvin">River Kelvin</a>, which flows from the <a href="/wiki/Campsie_Fells" title="Campsie Fells">Campsie Fells</a> in the north and confluences with the River Clyde at Yorkhill Quay.\n</p><p>The spire of <a href="/wiki/George_Gilbert_Scott" title="George Gilbert Scott">Sir George Gilbert Scott</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">Glasgow University</a> main building (the second largest <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic Revival">Gothic Revival</a> building in Great Britain) is a major landmark, and can be seen from miles around, sitting atop Gilmorehill. The university itself is the fourth oldest in the <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a>. Much of the city\'s student population is based in the West End, adding to its cultural vibrancy.\n</p><p>The area is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Art_Gallery_and_Museum" title="Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum">Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunterian_Museum_and_Art_Gallery" title="Hunterian Museum and Art Gallery">Hunterian Museum and Art Gallery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvin_Hall_International_Sports_Arena" title="Kelvin Hall International Sports Arena">Kelvin Hall International Sports Arena</a> and the Henry Wood Hall (home of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scottish_National_Orchestra" title="Royal Scottish National Orchestra">Royal Scottish National Orchestra</a> although they generally perform at the Glasgow Royal Concert Hall). Adjacent to the Kelvin Hall was the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Museum_of_Transport" title="Glasgow Museum of Transport">Museum of Transport</a>, which reopened in 2010 after moving to a new location on a former dockland site at <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Harbour" title="Glasgow Harbour">Glasgow Harbour</a> where the River Kelvin flows into the Clyde. The new building is built to a design by <a href="/wiki/Zaha_Hadid" title="Zaha Hadid">Zaha Hadid</a>. The <a href="/wiki/West_End_Festival" title="West End Festival">West End Festival</a>, one of Glasgow\'s largest festivals, is held annually in June.\n</p><p>Glasgow is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Exhibition_and_Conference_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre">SECC</a>, Great Britain\'s largest exhibition and conference centre.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> On 30 September 2013, a major expansion of the SECC facilities at the former Queen\'s Dock by <a href="/wiki/Foster_and_Partners" title="Foster and Partners">Foster and Partners</a> officially opened \xe2\x80\x93 the 13,000 seat <a href="/wiki/The_Hydro" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hydro">Hydro</a> arena.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_End">East End</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: East End">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens,_Glasgow_Green.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens%2C_Glasgow_Green.JPG/250px-People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens%2C_Glasgow_Green.JPG" width="250" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens%2C_Glasgow_Green.JPG/375px-People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens%2C_Glasgow_Green.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens%2C_Glasgow_Green.JPG/500px-People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens%2C_Glasgow_Green.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2521" data-file-height="1821" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:People%27s_Palace_and_Winter_Gardens,_Glasgow_Green.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Palace,_Glasgow" title="People&#39;s Palace, Glasgow">People\'s Palace</a> museum on <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Green" title="Glasgow Green">Glasgow Green</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The East End extends from <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cross" title="Glasgow Cross">Glasgow Cross</a> in the <a href="/wiki/City_Centre_of_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="City Centre of Glasgow">City Centre</a> to the boundary with <a href="/wiki/North_Lanarkshire" title="North Lanarkshire">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Lanarkshire" title="South Lanarkshire">South Lanarkshire</a>. It is home to the famous <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Barrowland_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Barrowland market">Glasgow Barrowland market</a>, popularly known as "The Barras",<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barrowland_Ballroom" title="Barrowland Ballroom">Barrowland Ballroom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Green" title="Glasgow Green">Glasgow Green</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Celtic Park</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic FC</a>. Many of the original sandstone tenements remain in this district. The East End was once a major industrial centre, home to <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Arrol_%26_Co." title="Sir William Arrol &amp; Co.">Sir William Arrol &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Templeton_%26_Co" title="James Templeton &amp; Co">James Templeton &amp; Co</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Beardmore_and_Company" title="William Beardmore and Company">William Beardmore and Company</a>. A notable local employer continues to be the <a href="/wiki/Wellpark_Brewery" title="Wellpark Brewery">Wellpark Brewery</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Tennent%27s_Lager" class="mw-redirect" title="Tennent&#39;s Lager">Tennent\'s Lager</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Necropolis" title="Glasgow Necropolis">Glasgow Necropolis</a> Cemetery was created by the Merchants House on a hill above the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cathedral" title="Glasgow Cathedral">cathedral</a> in 1831. Routes curve through the landscape uphill to the 62-metre (203&#160;ft) high statue of <a href="/wiki/John_Knox" title="John Knox">John Knox</a> at the summit. There are two late 18th century tenements in Gallowgate. Dating from 1771 and 1780, both have been well restored. The construction of Charlotte Street was financed by <a href="/wiki/David_Dale" title="David Dale">David Dale</a>, whose former pretensions can be gauged by the one remaining house, now run by the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Scotland" title="National Trust for Scotland">National Trust for Scotland</a>. Further along Charlotte Street there stands a modern <a href="/wiki/Gillespie,_Kidd_%26_Coia" title="Gillespie, Kidd &amp; Coia">Gillespie, Kidd &amp; Coia</a> building of some note. Once a school, it has been converted into offices. Surrounding these buildings are a series of innovative housing developments conceived as "Homes for the Future", part of a project during the city\'s year as UK City of Architecture and Design in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>East of Glasgow Cross is <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew%27s_in_the_Square" title="St Andrew&#39;s in the Square">St Andrew\'s in the Square</a>, the oldest post-Reformation church in Scotland, built in 1739\xe2\x80\x931757 and displaying a Presbyterian grandeur befitting the church of the city\'s wealthy <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Lords" title="Tobacco Lords">tobacco merchants</a>. Also close by is the more modest <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Episcopalian</a> <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew%27s-by-the-Green" title="St Andrew&#39;s-by-the-Green">St Andrew\'s-by-the-Green</a>, the oldest Episcopal church in Scotland. The Episcopalian St Andrew\'s was also known as the "Whistlin\' Kirk" due to it being the first church after the Reformation to own an organ.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg/250px-Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg" width="250" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg/375px-Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg/500px-Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="393" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Doulton_Fountain_-_Glasgow_Green.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Doulton_Fountain" class="mw-redirect" title="Doulton Fountain">Doulton Fountain</a> in Glasgow Green</div></div></div>\n<p>Overlooking Glasgow Green is the fa\xc3\xa7ade of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Templeton_on_the_Green&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Templeton on the Green (page does not exist)">Templeton on the Green</a>, featuring vibrant <a href="/wiki/Polychrome" title="Polychrome">polychromatic</a> brickwork intended to evoke the <a href="/wiki/Doge%27s_Palace,_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Doge&#39;s Palace, Venice">Doge\'s Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The extensive <a href="/wiki/Tollcross,_Glasgow" title="Tollcross, Glasgow">Tollcross Park</a> was originally developed from the estate of James Dunlop, the owner of a local steelworks. His large <a href="/wiki/Scots_Baronial_Style_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Baronial Style architecture">baronial</a> mansion was built in 1848 by <a href="/wiki/David_Bryce" title="David Bryce">David Bryce</a>, which later housed the city\'s Children\'s Museum until the 1980s. Today, the mansion is a sheltered housing complex.\n</p><p>The new <a href="/wiki/National_Indoor_Sports_Arena_and_Sir_Chris_Hoy_Velodrome" class="mw-redirect" title="National Indoor Sports Arena and Sir Chris Hoy Velodrome">Scottish National Indoor Sports Arena</a>, a modern replacement for the <a href="/wiki/Kelvin_Hall" title="Kelvin Hall">Kelvin Hall</a>, is in <a href="/wiki/Dalmarnock" title="Dalmarnock">Dalmarnock</a>. The area was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Village" title="Olympic Village">Athletes\' Village</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="2014 Commonwealth Games">2014 Commonwealth Games</a>, located adjacent to the new indoor sports arena.\n</p><p>To the north of the East End lie the two massive <a href="/wiki/Gasometer" class="mw-redirect" title="Gasometer">gasometers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Provan_Gas_Works" title="Provan Gas Works">Provan Gas Works</a>, which stand overlooking <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Park,_Glasgow" title="Alexandra Park, Glasgow">Alexandra Park</a> and a major interchange between the M8 and <a href="/wiki/M80_motorway" title="M80 motorway">M80</a> motorways. Often used for displaying large city advertising slogans, the towers have become an unofficial portal into the city for road users arriving from the north and east.\n</p><p>The <i>East End Healthy Living Centre</i> (EEHLC) was established in mid-2005 at Crownpoint Road with Lottery Funding and City grants to serve community needs in the area. Now called the <i>Glasgow Club Crownpoint Sports Complex</i>, the centre provides service such as sports facilities, health advice, stress management, leisure and vocational classes.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Side">South Side</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: South Side">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Glasgow\'s South Side sprawls out south of the Clyde. The urban area includes some of Greater Glasgow\'s most affluent suburbs such as <a href="/wiki/Newton_Mearns" title="Newton Mearns">Newton Mearns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitecraigs" class="mw-redirect" title="Whitecraigs">Whitecraigs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarkston,_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="Clarkston, Glasgow">Clarkston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giffnock" title="Giffnock">Giffnock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thorntonhall" title="Thorntonhall">Thorntonhall</a>, all of which are outside the city boundaries in <a href="/wiki/East_Renfrewshire" title="East Renfrewshire">East Renfrewshire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Newlands,_Glasgow" title="Newlands, Glasgow">Newlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dumbreck" title="Dumbreck">Dumbreck</a> are examples of high-value residential districts within the city boundaries. There are many areas containing a high concentration of sandstone tenements, examples being <a href="/wiki/Battlefield,_Glasgow" title="Battlefield, Glasgow">Battlefield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Govanhill" title="Govanhill">Govanhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Florida" title="Mount Florida">Mount Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shawlands" title="Shawlands">Shawlands</a>. The large suburb of <a href="/wiki/Pollokshields" title="Pollokshields">Pollokshields</a> comprises both a quiet western part with undulating tree-lined boulevards lined with expensive villas, and a busier eastern part with a high-density grid of tenements and small shops. The south side also includes some post-war housing estates of various sizes such as <a href="/wiki/Toryglen" title="Toryglen">Toryglen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pollok" title="Pollok">Pollok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castlemilk" title="Castlemilk">Castlemilk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arden,_Glasgow" title="Arden, Glasgow">Arden</a>.\n</p><p>The towns of <a href="/wiki/Cambuslang" title="Cambuslang">Cambuslang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutherglen" title="Rutherglen">Rutherglen</a> were included in the City of Glasgow district from 1975 to 1996, but are now in the <a href="/wiki/South_Lanarkshire" title="South Lanarkshire">South Lanarkshire</a> council area.\n</p><p>Although predominantly residential, the area does have several notable public buildings including, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh" title="Charles Rennie Mackintosh">Charles Rennie Mackintosh</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Street_School_Museum" title="Scotland Street School Museum">Scotland Street School Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_for_an_Art_Lover" title="House for an Art Lover">House for an Art Lover</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Burrell_Collection" title="Burrell Collection">Burrell Collection</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pollok_Country_Park" title="Pollok Country Park">Pollok Country Park</a>; <a href="/wiki/Alexander_%22Greek%22_Thomson" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander &quot;Greek&quot; Thomson">Alexander "Greek" Thomson</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Holmwood_House" title="Holmwood House">Holmwood House</a> villa; the National Football Stadium <a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Florida" title="Mount Florida">Mount Florida</a> (home of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queens Park FC</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Ibrox_Stadium" title="Ibrox Stadium">Ibrox Stadium</a> (home of <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers FC</a>).\n</p><p>The former docklands site at <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Quay" title="Pacific Quay">Pacific Quay</a> on the south bank of the River Clyde, opposite the SECC, is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Science_Centre" title="Glasgow Science Centre">Glasgow Science Centre</a> and the new headquarters for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">BBC Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/STV_Group_(Scotland)" title="STV Group (Scotland)">STV Group</a> (owner of <a href="/wiki/STV_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="STV (TV network)">STV</a>), which have relocated there to a new purpose built digital media campus.\n</p><p>In addition, several new bridges spanning the River Clyde have been built or are currently planned, including the <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Arc" title="Clyde Arc">Clyde Arc</a> known by locals as the Squinty Bridge at <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Quay" title="Pacific Quay">Pacific Quay</a> and others at <a href="/wiki/Tradeston" title="Tradeston">Tradeston</a> and Springfield Quay.\n</p><p>The South Side also includes many public parks, including <a href="/wiki/Linn_Park,_Glasgow,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Linn Park, Glasgow, Scotland">Linn Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park,_Glasgow" title="Queen&#39;s Park, Glasgow">Queen\'s Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellahouston_Park" title="Bellahouston Park">Bellahouston Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rouken_Glen" class="mw-redirect" title="Rouken Glen">Rouken Glen Park</a>, and several golf clubs, including the championship course at <a href="/wiki/Haggs_Castle" title="Haggs Castle">Haggs Castle</a>. The South Side is also home to <a href="/wiki/Pollok_Country_Park" title="Pollok Country Park">Pollok Country Park</a>, which was awarded the accolade of Europe\'s Best Park 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Pollok Park is Glasgow\'s largest park and the only country park within the city boundaries.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Govan" title="Govan">Govan</a> is a district and former burgh in the south-western part of the city. It is situated on the south bank of the River Clyde, opposite <a href="/wiki/Partick" title="Partick">Partick</a>. It was an administratively independent Police Burgh from 1864 until it was incorporated into the expanding city of Glasgow in 1912. Govan has a legacy as an engineering and <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> centre of international repute and is home to one of two <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Surface_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Surface Ships">BAE Systems Surface Ships shipyards</a> on the River Clyde and the <a href="/wiki/Precision_engineering" title="Precision engineering">precision engineering</a> firm, <a href="/wiki/Thales_Optronics" title="Thales Optronics">Thales Optronics</a>. It is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_University_Hospital" title="Queen Elizabeth University Hospital">Queen Elizabeth University Hospital</a>, one of the largest hospitals in the country, and the maintenance depot for the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Subway" title="Glasgow Subway">Glasgow Subway</a> system. The wider Govan area includes the districts of <a href="/wiki/Ibrox,_Glasgow" title="Ibrox, Glasgow">Ibrox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kinning_Park" title="Kinning Park">Kinning Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cessnock,_Glasgow" title="Cessnock, Glasgow">Cessnock</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Glasgow">North Glasgow</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: North Glasgow">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg/250px-Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg/375px-Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg/500px-Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1903" data-file-height="1410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruchill_Church_at_canal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ruchill_Church_Hall" title="Ruchill Church Hall">Ruchill Church</a>, seen from the <a href="/wiki/Forth_and_Clyde_Canal" title="Forth and Clyde Canal">Forth and Clyde Canal</a></div></div></div>\n<p>North Glasgow extends out from the north of the city centre towards the affluent suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Bearsden" title="Bearsden">Bearsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milngavie" title="Milngavie">Milngavie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishopbriggs" title="Bishopbriggs">Bishopbriggs</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Dunbartonshire" title="East Dunbartonshire">East Dunbartonshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clydebank" title="Clydebank">Clydebank</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Dunbartonshire" title="West Dunbartonshire">West Dunbartonshire</a>. The area also contains some of the city\'s poorest residential areas. <a href="/wiki/Possilpark" title="Possilpark">Possilpark</a> is one such district, where levels of unemployment and drug abuse continue to be above the national average. Much of the housing in areas such as Possilpark and <a href="/wiki/Hamiltonhill" title="Hamiltonhill">Hamiltonhill</a> have fallen into a state of disrepair in recent years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>This has led to large scale redevelopment of much of the poorer housing stock in north Glasgow, and the wider regeneration of many areas, such as <a href="/wiki/Ruchill" title="Ruchill">Ruchill</a>, which have been transformed; many run-down tenements have now been refurbished or replaced by modern <a href="/wiki/Housing_estate" title="Housing estate">housing estates</a>. Much of the housing stock in north Glasgow is rented <a href="/wiki/Social_housing" class="mw-redirect" title="Social housing">social housing</a>, with a high proportion of high-rise tower blocks, managed by the North Glasgow Housing Association trading as NG Homes and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Housing_Association" title="Glasgow Housing Association">Glasgow Housing Association</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maryhill" title="Maryhill">Maryhill</a> consists of well maintained traditional sandstone tenements. Although historically a working class area, its borders with the upmarket West End of the city mean that it is relatively wealthy compared to the rest of the north of the city, containing affluent areas such as <a href="/wiki/Maryhill_Park" title="Maryhill Park">Maryhill Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Kelvinside" title="North Kelvinside">North Kelvinside</a>. Maryhill is also the location of <a href="/wiki/Firhill_Stadium" title="Firhill Stadium">Firhill Stadium</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Partick_Thistle_F.C." title="Partick Thistle F.C.">Partick Thistle F.C.</a> since 1909. The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Junior_Football_Association" title="Scottish Junior Football Association">junior</a> team, <a href="/wiki/Maryhill_F.C." title="Maryhill F.C.">Maryhill F.C.</a> are also located in this part of north Glasgow.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Forth_and_Clyde_Canal" title="Forth and Clyde Canal">Forth and Clyde Canal</a> passes through this part of the city, and at one stage formed a vital part of the local economy. It was for many years polluted and largely unused after the decline of heavy industry, but recent efforts to regenerate and re-open the canal to navigation have seen it rejuvenated.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sighthill,_Glasgow" title="Sighthill, Glasgow">Sighthill</a> was home to Scotland\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Asylum_seeker" title="Asylum seeker">asylum seeker</a> community but the area is now regenerated as part of the Youth Olympic Games bid.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A huge part of the economic life of Glasgow was once located in <a href="/wiki/Springburn" title="Springburn">Springburn</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Saracen_Foundry" title="Saracen Foundry">Saracen Foundry</a>, engineering works of firms like <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tennant" title="Charles Tennant">Charles Tennant</a> and locomotive workshops employed many Glaswegians. Indeed, Glasgow dominated this type of manufacturing, with 25% of all the world\'s locomotives being built in the area at one stage. It was home to the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/North_British_Locomotive_Company" title="North British Locomotive Company">North British Locomotive Company</a>. Today part of the <a href="/wiki/St._Rollox_railway_works" title="St. Rollox railway works">St. Rollox railway works</a> continues in use as a railway maintenance facility, all that is left of the industry in Springburn.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_in_Glasgow" title="Culture in Glasgow">Culture in Glasgow</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg/250px-Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg" width="250" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg/375px-Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg/500px-Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3564" data-file-height="2020" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mitchell_Library_at_night_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Established by wealthy tobacco merchant Stephen Mitchell, the <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Library" title="Mitchell Library">Mitchell Library</a> is now one of the largest public reference libraries in Europe.</div></div></div>\n<p>The city has many amenities for a wide range of cultural activities, from <a href="/wiki/Curling" title="Curling">curling</a> to opera and ballet and from <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> to art appreciation; it also has a large selection of museums that include those devoted to transport, religion, and <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a>. Many of the city\'s cultural sites were celebrated in 1990 when Glasgow was designated <a href="/wiki/European_City_of_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="European City of Culture">European City of Culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s principal municipal library, the <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Library" title="Mitchell Library">Mitchell Library</a>, has grown into one of the largest public reference <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">libraries</a> in Europe, currently housing some 1.3&#160;million books, an extensive collection of newspapers and thousands of photographs and <a href="/wiki/Map" title="Map">maps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\nOf academic libraries, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_University_Library" title="Glasgow University Library">Glasgow University Library</a> started in the 15th century and is one of the oldest and largest libraries in Europe, with unique and distinctive collections of international status.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of Scotland\'s national arts organisations are based in Glasgow, including <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Opera" title="Scottish Opera">Scottish Opera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Ballet" title="Scottish Ballet">Scottish Ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_of_Scotland" title="National Theatre of Scotland">National Theatre of Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scottish_National_Orchestra" title="Royal Scottish National Orchestra">Royal Scottish National Orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scottish_Symphony_Orchestra" title="BBC Scottish Symphony Orchestra">BBC Scottish Symphony Orchestra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Youth_Theatre" title="Scottish Youth Theatre">Scottish Youth Theatre</a>.\n</p><p>Glasgow has its own "<a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Poet Laureate">Poet Laureate</a>", a post created in 1999 for <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Morgan_(poet)" title="Edwin Morgan (poet)">Edwin Morgan</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and occupied by <a href="/wiki/Liz_Lochhead" title="Liz Lochhead">Liz Lochhead</a> from 2005<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> until 2011, when she stood down to take up the position of Scots Makar.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Jim Carruth was appointed to the position of Poet Laureate for Glasgow in 2014 as part of the 2014 Commonwealth Games legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a> declared Glasgow to be the most vegan-friendly city in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Festivals">Glasgow Festivals</a></div>\n<p>Glasgow is home to a variety of theatres including the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Theatre,_Glasgow" title="King&#39;s Theatre, Glasgow">King\'s Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Glasgow" title="Theatre Royal, Glasgow">Theatre Royal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Theatre" title="Citizens Theatre">Citizens Theatre</a> and is home to many museums and art galleries, the largest and most famous being the <a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Art_Gallery_and_Museum" title="Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum">Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hunterian_Museum_and_Art_Gallery" title="Hunterian Museum and Art Gallery">Hunterian Museum and Art Gallery</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gallery_of_Modern_Art,_Glasgow" title="Gallery of Modern Art, Glasgow">Gallery of Modern Art</a> (GoMA) and the <a href="/wiki/Burrell_Collection" title="Burrell Collection">Burrell Collection</a>. Most of the museums and galleries in Glasgow are publicly owned and free to enter.\n</p><p>The city has hosted many exhibitions over the years, including being the UK City of Architecture 1999, <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> 1990, National City of Sport 1995\xe2\x80\x931999 and European Capital of Sport 2003. Glasgow has also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_M%C3%B2d" title="Royal National M\xc3\xb2d">National M\xc3\xb2d</a> no less than twelve times since 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-SMO_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMO-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition, unlike the older and larger <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Festival">Edinburgh Festival</a> (where all Edinburgh\'s main festivals occur in the last three weeks of August), Glasgow\'s festivals fill the calendar. Festivals include the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_International_Comedy_Festival" title="Glasgow International Comedy Festival">Glasgow International Comedy Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_International" title="Glasgow International">Glasgow International Festival of Visual Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_International_Jazz_Festival" title="Glasgow International Jazz Festival">Glasgow International Jazz Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Connections" title="Celtic Connections">Celtic Connections</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Fair" title="Glasgow Fair">Glasgow Fair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Film_Festival" title="Glasgow Film Festival">Glasgow Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_End_Festival" title="West End Festival">West End Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merchant_City_Festival" title="Merchant City Festival">Merchant City Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgay!_Festival" title="Glasgay! Festival">Glasgay</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Pipe_Band_Championships" title="World Pipe Band Championships">World Pipe Band Championships</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_scene">Music scene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music scene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_bands_from_Glasgow" title="List of bands from Glasgow">List of bands from Glasgow</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow,_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Glasgow%2C_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg/220px-Glasgow%2C_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Glasgow%2C_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg/330px-Glasgow%2C_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Glasgow%2C_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg/440px-Glasgow%2C_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow,_Royal_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1539279.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Glasgow Royal Concert Hall">Glasgow Royal Concert Hall</a></div></div></div><p>\nGlasgow has many live music venues, pubs, and clubs. Some of the city\'s more well-known venues include the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Glasgow Royal Concert Hall">Glasgow Royal Concert Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hydro" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hydro">The Hydro</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Exhibition_and_Conference_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre">SECC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cathouse" title="Glasgow Cathouse">Glasgow Cathouse</a>, The Art School, <a href="/wiki/King_Tut%27s_Wah_Wah_Hut" title="King Tut&#39;s Wah Wah Hut">King Tut\'s Wah Wah Hut</a> (where <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a> were spotted and signed by Glaswegian record mogul <a href="/wiki/Alan_McGee" title="Alan McGee">Alan McGee</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Margaret_Union" title="Queen Margaret Union">Queen Margaret Union</a> (who have <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">Kurt Cobain</a>\'s footprint locked in a safe), <a href="/wiki/Barrowland_Ballroom" title="Barrowland Ballroom">the Barrowland</a>, a ballroom converted into a live music venue as well as <a href="/wiki/The_Garage_(nightclub)" title="The Garage (nightclub)">The Garage</a>, which is the largest nightclub in Scotland.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg/220px-SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg/330px-SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg/440px-SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4864" data-file-height="2396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SSE_Hydro_in_Glasgow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/SSE_Hydro" title="SSE Hydro">SSE Hydro</a> arena</div></div></div><p> More recent mid-sized venues include <a href="/wiki/O2_ABC_Glasgow" title="O2 ABC Glasgow">ABC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/O2_Academy_Glasgow" title="O2 Academy Glasgow">O<sub>2</sub> Academy</a>, which play host to a similar range of acts. There are also a large number of smaller venues and bars, which host many local and touring musicians, including Stereo, 13th Note and Nice N Sleazy. Most recent recipient of the SLTN Music Pub of the Year award was Bar Bloc, awarded in November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Glasgow was named the UK\'s fourth "most musical" city by <a href="/wiki/PRS_for_Music" title="PRS for Music">PRS for Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mirror.co.uk_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirror.co.uk-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mirror.co.uk_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirror.co.uk-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Glasgow is also the "most mentioned city in the UK" in song titles, outside London according, to a chart produced by PRS for music, with 119, ahead of closest rivals Edinburgh who received 95 mentions<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent years<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2012)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, the success of bands such as <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Nile" title="The Blue Nile">The Blue Nile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gun_(band)" title="Gun (band)">Gun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simple_Minds" title="Simple Minds">Simple Minds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Del_Amitri" title="Del Amitri">Del Amitri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_(band)" title="Texas (band)">Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hipsway" title="Hipsway">Hipsway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Love_%26_Money" title="Love &amp; Money">Love &amp; Money</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idlewild_(band)" title="Idlewild (band)">Idlewild</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deacon_Blue" title="Deacon Blue">Deacon Blue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_Juice_(band)" title="Orange Juice (band)">Orange Juice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Cole_and_the_Commotions" title="Lloyd Cole and the Commotions">Lloyd Cole and the Commotions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teenage_Fanclub" title="Teenage Fanclub">Teenage Fanclub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belle_and_Sebastian" title="Belle and Sebastian">Belle and Sebastian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camera_Obscura_(band)" title="Camera Obscura (band)">Camera Obscura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Ferdinand_(band)" title="Franz Ferdinand (band)">Franz Ferdinand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mogwai" title="Mogwai">Mogwai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_(band)" title="Travis (band)">Travis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Primal_Scream" title="Primal Scream">Primal Scream</a> has significantly boosted the profile of the Glasgow music scene, prompting <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Magazine">Time Magazine</a></i> to liken Glasgow to <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> during its 1960s <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a> heyday.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> More recent<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2012)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> successes include <a href="/wiki/The_Fratellis" title="The Fratellis">The Fratellis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chvrches" title="Chvrches">Chvrches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rustie" title="Rustie">Rustie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasvegas" title="Glasvegas">Glasvegas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twin_Atlantic" title="Twin Atlantic">Twin Atlantic</a>. The city of Glasgow was appointed a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> City of Music on 20 August 2008 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network" title="Creative Cities Network">Creative Cities Network</a>.\n</p><p>Glasgow\'s contemporary dance music scene has been spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Slam_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Slam (band)">Slam</a>, and their record label <a href="/wiki/Soma_Quality_Recordings" title="Soma Quality Recordings">Soma Quality Recordings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> with their Pressure club nights attracting DJs and clubbers from around the world, which was previously held at <a href="/wiki/The_Arches_(Glasgow)" title="The Arches (Glasgow)">The Arches</a> but following that venue\'s closure due to claims of unsafe level of drug use has moved to Sub Club.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/MOBO_Awards" title="MOBO Awards">MOBO Awards</a> were held at the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Exhibition_and_Conference_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre">SECC</a> on 30 September 2009, making Glasgow the first out-of-London city to host the event since its launch in 1995. On 9 November 2014, Glasgow hosted the <a href="/wiki/2014_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2014 MTV Europe Music Awards">2014 MTV Europe Music Awards</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_SSE_Hydro" class="mw-redirect" title="The SSE Hydro">The SSE Hydro</a>, it was the second time Scotland hosted the show since 2003 in Edinburgh and overall the fifth time that the United Kingdom has hosted the show since 2011 in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. The event was hosted by <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and featured performances from <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Iglesias" title="Enrique Iglesias">Enrique Iglesias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a>, <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Glasgow" title="Media in Glasgow">Media in Glasgow</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Scotland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/BBC_Scotland.jpg/220px-BBC_Scotland.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/BBC_Scotland.jpg/330px-BBC_Scotland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/BBC_Scotland.jpg/440px-BBC_Scotland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Scotland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">BBC Scotland</a> HQ, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Quay" title="Pacific Quay">Pacific Quay</a>, Glasgow</div></div></div>\n<p>There have been hundreds of films made about Glasgow or in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Both <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">BBC Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/STV_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="STV (TV network)">STV</a> have their headquarters in Glasgow. Television programs filmed in Glasgow include <i><a href="/wiki/Rab_C._Nesbitt" title="Rab C. Nesbitt">Rab C.
