Nesbitt</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Taggart" title="Taggart">Taggart</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/High_Times_(TV_series)" title="High Times (TV series)">High Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/River_City" title="River City">River City</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/City_Lights_(TV_series)" title="City Lights (TV series)">City Lights</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chewin%27_the_Fat" title="Chewin&#39; the Fat">Chewin\' the Fat</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Still_Game" title="Still Game">Still Game</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lovesick_(TV_series)" title="Lovesick (TV series)">Lovesick</a></i>. Most recently the long-running series <i><a href="/wiki/Question_Time_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Question Time (TV series)">Question Time</a></i> and the early evening quiz programme <i><a href="/wiki/Eggheads_(TV_series)" title="Eggheads (TV series)">Eggheads</a></i> moved its production base to the city. Most National Lottery game shows are also filmed in Glasgow. children\'s game show <i><a href="/wiki/Copycats" title="Copycats">Copycats</a></i> is filmed there, and the Irish/UK programme <i><a href="/wiki/Mrs._Brown%27s_Boys" title="Mrs. Brown&#39;s Boys">Mrs. Brown\'s Boys</a></i> is filmed at BBC Scotland.\n</p><p>The Scottish press publishes various newspapers in the city such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Evening_Times" title="Evening Times">Evening Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Herald_(Glasgow)" title="The Herald (Glasgow)">The Herald</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Herald" title="Sunday Herald">The Sunday Herald</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Mail_(Scotland)" title="Sunday Mail (Scotland)">Sunday Mail</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Record_(Scotland)" title="Daily Record (Scotland)">Daily Record</a></i>. Scottish editions of <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Mirror" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Mirror">Trinity Mirror</a> and <a href="/wiki/News_International" class="mw-redirect" title="News International">News International</a> titles are printed in the city. <a href="/wiki/STV_Group_(Scotland)" title="STV Group (Scotland)">STV Group</a> is a Glasgow-based media conglomerate with interests in television, and publishing advertising. STV Group owns and operates both Scottish ITV franchises (Central Scotland and Grampian), both branded <a href="/wiki/STV_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="STV (TV network)">STV</a>. Glasgow also had its own television channel, <a href="/wiki/STV_Glasgow" title="STV Glasgow">STV Glasgow</a>, which launched in June 2014, which also shows some of Glasgow\'s own programs filmed at the STV headquarters in Glasgow. Shows included <i>The Riverside Show</i>, <i>Scottish Kitchen</i>, <i>City Safari</i>, <i>Football Show</i> and <i>Live at Five</i>. STV Glasgow merged with STV Edinburgh to form STV2 in April 2017 which eventually closed in June 2018.\n</p><p>Various radio stations are also located in Glasgow. <a href="/wiki/Bauer_Radio" title="Bauer Radio">Bauer Radio</a> owns the principal commercial radio stations in Glasgow: <a href="/wiki/102.5_Clyde_1" class="mw-redirect" title="102.5 Clyde 1">Clyde 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/1152_Clyde_2" class="mw-redirect" title="1152 Clyde 2">Clyde 2</a>, which can reach over 2.3&#160;million listeners.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, STV Group plc (then known as SMG plc) sold its 27.8% stake in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Radio_Holdings" title="Scottish Radio Holdings">Scottish Radio Holdings</a> to the broadcasting group <a href="/wiki/EMAP" class="mw-redirect" title="EMAP">EMAP</a> for \xc2\xa390.5&#160;million. Other stations broadcasting from Glasgow include <a href="/wiki/105.2_Smooth_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="105.2 Smooth Radio">105.2 Smooth Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Radio" title="Real Radio">Real Radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/96.3_Rock_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="96.3 Rock Radio">96.3 Rock Radio</a>, which are all owned by <a href="/wiki/GMG_Radio" title="GMG Radio">GMG Radio</a>. Global Radio\'s Central Scotland radio station <a href="/wiki/Capital_FM_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital FM Scotland">Capital FM Scotland</a> also broadcast from studios in Glasgow. The city has a strong <a href="/wiki/Community_radio" title="Community radio">community radio</a> sector, including <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Music_Radio" title="Celtic Music Radio">Celtic Music Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subcity_Radio" title="Subcity Radio">Subcity Radio</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radio_Magnetic&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Radio Magnetic (page does not exist)">Radio Magnetic</a>, Sunny Govan Radio, AWAZ FM and Insight Radio.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sectarianism_in_Glasgow" title="Sectarianism in Glasgow">Sectarianism in Glasgow</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg/170px-Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg" width="170" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg/255px-Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg/340px-Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="1624" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow-cathedral-may-2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Glasgow Cathedral marks the site where <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mungo" title="Saint Mungo">Saint Mungo</a> built his church and established Glasgow.</div></div></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:508px;max-width:508px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Protestant/Catholic divide in Glasgow (2011 census)</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png/250px-Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png" width="250" height="208" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png/375px-Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png/500px-Church_Of_Scotland_Glasgow_2011_census.png 2x" data-file-width="21134" data-file-height="17552" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Church of Scotland</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png/250px-Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png" width="250" height="208" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png/375px-Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png/500px-Roman_Catholic_Glasgow_2011_Census.png 2x" data-file-width="21065" data-file-height="17494" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Roman Catholic</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow is a city of significant religious diversity. The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Scotland">Roman Catholic Church</a> are the two largest Christian denominations in the city. There are 147 congregations in the Church of Scotland\'s <a href="/wiki/Presbytery_of_Glasgow_(Church_of_Scotland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbytery of Glasgow (Church of Scotland)">Presbytery of Glasgow</a> (of which 104 are within the city boundaries, the other 43 being in adjacent areas such as <a href="/wiki/Giffnock" title="Giffnock">Giffnock</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Within the city boundaries there are 65 parishes of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Glasgow" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Glasgow">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Glasgow</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and four parishes of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Motherwell" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Motherwell">Diocese of Motherwell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The city has four Christian <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">cathedrals</a>: <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cathedral" title="Glasgow Cathedral">Glasgow Cathedral</a>, of the Church of Scotland; <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew%27s_Cathedral,_Glasgow" title="St Andrew&#39;s Cathedral, Glasgow">St Andrew\'s Cathedral</a>, of the Roman Catholic Church; <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Cathedral,_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Mary&#39;s Cathedral, Glasgow">St Mary\'s Cathedral</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Scottish Episcopal Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St_Luke%27s_Orthodox_Cathedral,_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="St Luke&#39;s Orthodox Cathedral, Glasgow">St Luke\'s Cathedral</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox Church</a>.\n</p><p>32% of the population follow the Protestant Church of Scotland whilst 29% following the Roman Catholic Church, according to the 2001 census (Christians overall form 65%).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Much of the city\'s Catholic population are those of <a href="/wiki/Irish-Scots" title="Irish-Scots">Irish ancestry</a>. The large division between the two religions and its respective communities play a major part in <a href="/wiki/Sectarianism_in_Glasgow" title="Sectarianism in Glasgow">sectarianism in Glasgow</a>, in a similar nature to that of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Biblical_Unitarianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Biblical Unitarianism">Biblical unitarians</a> are represented by three <a href="/wiki/Christadelphian" class="mw-redirect" title="Christadelphian">Christadelphian</a> ecclesias, referred to geographically, as "South",<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> "Central"<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> and "Kelvin".<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a> community is served by 4 <a href="/wiki/Gurdwaras" class="mw-redirect" title="Gurdwaras">Gurdwaras</a>. Two are situated in the West End (<i>Central Gurdwara Singh Sabha</i> in <a href="/wiki/Finnieston" title="Finnieston">Finnieston</a> and <i>Guru Nanak Sikh Temple</i> in <a href="/wiki/Kelvinbridge" title="Kelvinbridge">Kelvinbridge</a>) and two in the Southside area of <a href="/wiki/Pollokshields" title="Pollokshields">Pollokshields</a> (<i>Guru Granth Sahib Gurdwara</i> and <i>Sri Guru Tegh Bahadur Gurdwara</i>). In 2013, Scotland\'s first purpose-built Gurdwara opened in a massive opening ceremony. Built at a cost of \xc2\xa33.8m it can hold 1500 worshippers.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Central Gurdwara is currently constructing a new building in the city. There are almost 10,000 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sikhs_in_Scotland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sikhs in Scotland (page does not exist)">Sikhs in Scotland</a> and the majority live in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_Mosque" title="Glasgow Central Mosque">Glasgow Central Mosque</a> in the Gorbals district is the largest mosque in Scotland and, along with twelve other mosques in the city, caters for the city\'s Muslim population, estimated to number 33,000.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Glasgow also has a Hindu <a href="/wiki/Mandir" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandir">mandir</a>.\n</p><p>Glasgow has seven synagogues with the seventh largest Jewish population in the United Kingdom after <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>, but once had a Jewish population second only to London, estimated at 20,000 in the Gorbals alone.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1993, the <a href="/wiki/St_Mungo_Museum_of_Religious_Life_and_Art" title="St Mungo Museum of Religious Life and Art">St Mungo Museum of Religious Life and Art</a> opened in Glasgow. It is believed to be the only public museum to examine all the world\'s major religious faiths.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Glaswegian</i>, otherwise known as the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_patter" title="Glasgow patter">Glasgow patter</a>, is a local variety of <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>.\n</p><p>Glaswegian is a dialect, more than an alternative pronunciation; words also change their meaning depending on context, e.g. "away" can mean "leaving" as in <i>A\'m away</i>, an instruction to stop being a nuisance as in <i>away wi ye</i>, or "drunk" or "demented" as in <i>he\'s away wi it</i>. <i>Ginger</i> is a term for any carbonated soft drink, historically referring to <a href="/wiki/Ginger_beer" title="Ginger beer">ginger beer</a> (<i>A bottle o ginger</i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x99 \xcb\x88bo\xca\x94l \xc9\x99 \xcb\x88d\xca\x92\xc9\xaand\xca\x92\xc9\x99r]</a></span>). Then there are words whose meaning has no obvious relationship to that in standard English: <i>coupon</i> means "face", via "to punch a ticket coupon". A <a href="/wiki/Headbutt" title="Headbutt">headbutt</a> is known in many parts of the British Isles as a "Glasgow kiss", although this term is rarely used by Glaswegians, who say "Malkie", e.g., "ah\'ll Malkie ye" or "stick the heid/nut on ye".\n</p><p>A speaker of Glaswegian might refer to those originating from the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Isles" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Isles">Western Isles</a> as <i><a href="/wiki/Teuchter" title="Teuchter">teuchters</a></i>, while they would reciprocate by referring to Glaswegians as <i>keelies</i>. More recently, the word <i>weegie</i> has become more widely used to describe Glaswegians.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The long-running TV drama <i><a href="/wiki/Taggart" title="Taggart">Taggart</a></i> and the comedies <i><a href="/wiki/Empty_(TV_series)" title="Empty (TV series)">Empty</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chewin%27_the_Fat" title="Chewin&#39; the Fat">Chewin\' the Fat</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rab_C._Nesbitt" title="Rab C. Nesbitt">Rab C. Nesbitt</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Still_Game" title="Still Game">Still Game</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Limmy%27s_Show" title="Limmy&#39;s Show">Limmy\'s Show</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dear_Green_Place" title="Dear Green Place">Dear Green Place</a></i> depict the Glaswegian <i><a href="/wiki/Patois" title="Patois">patois</a></i>, while <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Bridges" title="Kevin Bridges">Kevin Bridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Boyle" title="Frankie Boyle">Frankie Boyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Ferguson" title="Craig Ferguson">Craig Ferguson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Connolly" title="Billy Connolly">Billy Connolly</a> have made Glaswegian humour known to the rest of the world.\n</p><p>Glasgow is Scotland\'s main locus of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a> language use outside the <a href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands" title="Highlands and Islands">Highlands and Islands</a>. In 2011, 5,878 residents of the city over age 3 spoke Gaelic, amounting to 1.0% of the population. Of Scotland\'s 25 largest cities, only <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a>, the unofficial capital of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Highlands</a>, has a larger percentage of Gaelic speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Glasgow" title="Greater Glasgow">Greater Glasgow</a> area there were 8,899 Gaelic-speakers or 0.8% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Both the Gaelic language television station <a href="/wiki/BBC_Alba" title="BBC Alba">BBC Alba</a> and the Gaelic language radio station <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_nan_G%C3%A0idheal" title="BBC Radio nan G\xc3\xa0idheal">BBC Radio nan G\xc3\xa0idheal</a> have studios in Glasgow, their only locations outside the <a href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands" title="Highlands and Islands">Highlands and Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_in_Glasgow" title="Architecture in Glasgow">Architecture in Glasgow</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clyde_Auditorium,_Glasgow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Clyde_Auditorium%2C_Glasgow.jpg/220px-Clyde_Auditorium%2C_Glasgow.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Clyde_Auditorium%2C_Glasgow.jpg/330px-Clyde_Auditorium%2C_Glasgow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Clyde_Auditorium%2C_Glasgow.jpg/440px-Clyde_Auditorium%2C_Glasgow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="851" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clyde_Auditorium,_Glasgow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lord_Foster" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Foster">Lord Foster</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Auditorium" class="mw-redirect" title="Clyde Auditorium">Clyde Auditorium</a>, colloquially known as \'the Armadillo\'</div></div></div>\n<p>Very little of <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> Glasgow remains; the two main landmarks from this period being the 15th century <a href="/wiki/Provand%27s_Lordship" title="Provand&#39;s Lordship">Provand\'s Lordship</a> and 13th century <a href="/wiki/St._Mungo%27s_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Mungo&#39;s Cathedral">St. Mungo\'s Cathedral</a>, although the original medieval street plan (along with many of the street names) on the eastern side of the city centre has largely survived intact. The vast majority of the city as seen today dates from the 19th century. As a result, Glasgow has an impressive heritage of <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian architecture</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Chambers" title="Glasgow City Chambers">Glasgow City Chambers</a>; the main building of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/George_Gilbert_Scott" title="George Gilbert Scott">Sir George Gilbert Scott</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Art_Gallery_and_Museum" title="Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum">Kelvingrove Art Gallery and Museum</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/John_William_Simpson_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="John William Simpson (architect)">Sir John W. Simpson</a>, are notable examples.\n</p><p>The city is notable for architecture designed by the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_School" title="Glasgow School">Glasgow School</a>, the most notable exponent of that style being <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh" title="Charles Rennie Mackintosh">Charles Rennie Mackintosh</a>. Mackintosh was an architect and designer in the <a href="/wiki/Arts_and_Crafts_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Arts and Crafts Movement">Arts and Crafts Movement</a> and the main exponent of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> in the United Kingdom, designing numerous noted Glasgow buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_School_of_Art" title="Glasgow School of Art">Glasgow School of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willow_Tearooms" title="Willow Tearooms">Willow Tearooms</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Street_School_Museum" title="Scotland Street School Museum">Scotland Street School Museum</a>. A hidden gem of Glasgow, also designed by Mackintosh, is the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Cross_Church,_Glasgow" title="Queen&#39;s Cross Church, Glasgow">Queen\'s Cross Church</a>, the only church by the renowned artist to be built.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another architect who has had an enduring impact on the city\'s appearance was <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Thomson" title="Alexander Thomson">Alexander Thomson</a>, with notable examples including the <a href="/wiki/Holmwood_House" title="Holmwood House">Holmwood House</a> villa, and likewise Sir <a href="/wiki/John_James_Burnet" title="John James Burnet">John James Burnet</a> who was awarded the R.I.B.A\'s Royal Gold Medal for his lifetime\'s service to architecture. The buildings reflect the wealth and self-confidence of the residents of the "Second City of the Empire". Glasgow generated immense wealth from trade and the industries that developed from the Industrial Revolution. The <a href="/wiki/Shipyard" title="Shipyard">shipyards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naval_architecture" title="Naval architecture">marine engineering</a>, steel making, and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a> all contributed to the growth of the city.\n</p><p>Many of the city\'s most impressive buildings were built with red or blond <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a>, but during the industrial era those colours disappeared under a pervasive black layer of soot and pollutants from the <a href="/wiki/Furnace" title="Furnace">furnaces</a>, until the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_1956" title="Clean Air Act 1956">Clean Air Act</a> was introduced in 1956. In recent years many of these buildings have been cleaned and restored to their original appearance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are over 1,800 listed buildings in the city, of architectural and historical importance, and 23 Conservation Areas extending over 1,471 hectares. Such areas include the Central Area, Dennistoun, the West End, Pollokshields \xe2\x80\x93 the first major planned garden suburb in Britain \xe2\x80\x93 Newlands and Carmunnock Village.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow,_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Glasgow%2C_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg/220px-Glasgow%2C_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Glasgow%2C_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg/330px-Glasgow%2C_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Glasgow%2C_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg/440px-Glasgow%2C_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow,_new_offices_and_square_trees_on_Broomielaw_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1534075.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New office builds in the city centre of Glasgow</div></div></div>\n<p>Modern buildings in Glasgow include the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Royal_Concert_Hall" title="Glasgow Royal Concert Hall">Glasgow Royal Concert Hall</a>, and along the banks of the Clyde are the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Science_Centre" title="Glasgow Science Centre">Glasgow Science Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hydro" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hydro">The Hydro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Exhibition_and_Conference_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre">Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Auditorium" class="mw-redirect" title="Clyde Auditorium">Clyde Auditorium</a> was designed by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Foster (architect)">Sir Norman Foster</a>, and is colloquially known as the "<a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">Armadillo</a>". In 2006 <a href="/wiki/Zaha_Hadid" title="Zaha Hadid">Zaha Hadid</a> won a competition to design the new <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Museum_of_Transport" title="Glasgow Museum of Transport">Museum of Transport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Hadid\'s museum opened on the waterfront in 2011 and has been renamed the <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Museum" title="Riverside Museum">Riverside Museum</a> to reflect the change in location and to celebrate Glasgow\'s rich industrial heritage stemming from the Clyde.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Glasgow\'s impressive historical and modern architectural traditions were celebrated in 1999 when the city was designated UK City of Architecture and Design,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> winning the accolade over <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG/250px-HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG/375px-HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG/500px-HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="567" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Daring_at_Scotstoun.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Daring_(D32)" title="HMS Daring (D32)">HMS <i>Daring</i></a> was built by <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Maritime_-_Naval_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Maritime - Naval Ships">BAE Systems Maritime - Naval Ships</a> in Glasgow and launched in 2006. Although diminished from its early 20th century heights, Glasgow remains the hub of the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> industry.</div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow has the largest <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Scotland" title="Economy of Scotland">economy in Scotland</a> and is at the hub of the metropolitan area of West Central Scotland. Glasgow also has the third highest GDP Per capita of any city in the UK (after London and Edinburgh).<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The city itself sustains more than 410,000 jobs in over 12,000 companies. Over 153,000 jobs were created in the city between 2000 and 2005&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 a growth rate of 32%.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Glasgow\'s annual economic growth rate of 4.4% is now second only to that of London. In 2005, over 17,000 new jobs were created, and 2006 saw private-sector investment in the city reaching \xc2\xa34.2&#160;billion, an increase of 22% in a single year.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> 55% of the residents in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Glasgow" title="Greater Glasgow">Greater Glasgow</a> area commute to the city every day. Once dominant export orientated manufacturing industries such as shipbuilding and other heavy engineering have been gradually replaced in importance by more diversified forms of economic activity, although major manufacturing firms continue to be headquartered in the city, such as <a href="/wiki/Aggreko" title="Aggreko">Aggreko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weir_Group" title="Weir Group">Weir Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_McColl" title="Jim McColl">Clyde Blowers</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Howden" title="James Howden">Howden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linn_Products" title="Linn Products">Linn Products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firebrand_Games" title="Firebrand Games">Firebrand Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Grant_%26_Sons" title="William Grant &amp; Sons">William Grant &amp; Sons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whyte_and_Mackay" class="mw-redirect" title="Whyte and Mackay">Whyte and Mackay</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Edrington_Group" title="The Edrington Group">The Edrington Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Polar_Engines" title="British Polar Engines">British Polar Engines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albion_Motors" title="Albion Motors">Albion Motors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Glasgow was once one of the most significant cities in the UK for manufacturing, which generated a great deal of the city\'s wealth; the most prominent industry being shipbuilding based on the River Clyde.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Although Glasgow owed much of its economic growth to the shipbuilding industry, which still continues today in the form of <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Maritime_-_Naval_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Maritime - Naval Ships">BAE Systems Maritime - Naval Ships</a>\' two shipyards, the city has its roots in the tobacco trade and is noted to have "risen from its medieval slumber" from trade in tobacco, pioneered by figures such as <a href="/wiki/John_Glassford" title="John Glassford">John Glassford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The city was also noted for its locomotive construction industry\xe2\x80\x94led by firms such as the <a href="/wiki/North_British_Locomotive_Company" title="North British Locomotive Company">North British Locomotive Company</a>\xe2\x80\x94which grew during the 19th century before entering a decline in the 1960s.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg/220px-Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg/330px-Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg/440px-Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1792" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Science_Centre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Tower" title="Glasgow Tower">Glasgow Tower</a>, Scotland\'s tallest tower, and the <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> Cinema at the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Science_Centre" title="Glasgow Science Centre">Glasgow Science Centre</a> symbolise the increase in the importance of tourism to the city\'s economy.</div></div></div>\n<p>Whilst manufacturing has declined, Glasgow\'s economy has seen significant relative growth of <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary</a> sector industries such as financial and business services, communications, <a href="/wiki/Biosciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosciences">biosciences</a>, creative industries, healthcare, higher education, retail and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Glasgow is now the second most popular foreign tourist destination in Scotland (fifth in the UK)<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> and offers Scotland\'s largest retail centre.\n</p><p>Between 1998 and 2001, the city\'s financial services sector grew at a rate of 30%, making considerable gains on Edinburgh, which has historically been the centre of the Scottish financial sector.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Glasgow is now one of Europe\'s sixteen largest financial centres,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> with a growing number of <a href="/wiki/Blue_chip_(stock_market)" title="Blue chip (stock market)">Blue chip</a> financial sector companies establishing significant operations or headquarters in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1990s and first decade of the 21st century saw substantial growth in the number of <a href="/wiki/Call_centre" title="Call centre">call centres</a> based in Glasgow. In 2007 roughly 20,000 people, a third of all call centre employees in Scotland, were employed by Glasgow call centres.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> This growth and its high use of recruitment agencies to hire graduates as temporary workers has led to accusations of exploitative practices such as long hours, poor pay and lack of job security by the <a href="/wiki/Trades_Union_Congress" title="Trades Union Congress">TUC</a> and other union bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In recent years some call centres have taken steps to rectify this criticism.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s main manufacturing industries include companies involved in; shipbuilding, engineering, construction, brewing and distilling, printing and publishing, chemicals and textiles as well as newer growth sectors such as <a href="/wiki/Optoelectronics" title="Optoelectronics">optoelectronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Glasgow forms the western part of the <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Glen" title="Silicon Glen">Silicon Glen</a> high tech sector of Scotland.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Glasgow" title="Transport in Glasgow">Transport in Glasgow</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG/220px-AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG/330px-AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG/440px-AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AM_Glasgow_Central.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central station</a> is the northern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_(1999-2000)._Killermont_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_%281999-2000%29._Killermont_Street.jpg/220px-Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_%281999-2000%29._Killermont_Street.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_%281999-2000%29._Killermont_Street.jpg/330px-Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_%281999-2000%29._Killermont_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_%281999-2000%29._Killermont_Street.jpg/440px-Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_%281999-2000%29._Killermont_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3928" data-file-height="2947" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow._George_Wyllie_-_%22The_Clyde_Clock%22_(1999-2000)._Killermont_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iconic <i>The Clyde Clock</i> outside Buchanan bus station</div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow has a large urban transport system, mostly managed by the <a href="/wiki/Strathclyde_Partnership_for_Transport" title="Strathclyde Partnership for Transport">Strathclyde Partnership for Transport</a> (SPT).\n</p><p>The city has many bus services; since <a href="/wiki/Bus_deregulation_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Bus deregulation in the United Kingdom">bus deregulation</a> almost all are provided by private operators though SPT part-funds some services. The principal bus operators within the city are: <a href="/wiki/First_Glasgow" title="First Glasgow">First Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill%27s_Bus_Services" title="McGill&#39;s Bus Services">McGill\'s Bus Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_West_Scotland" title="Stagecoach West Scotland">Stagecoach West Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Citybus" title="Glasgow Citybus">Glasgow Citybus</a>. The main bus terminal in the city is <a href="/wiki/Buchanan_bus_station" title="Buchanan bus station">Buchanan bus station</a>.\n</p><p>Glasgow has the most extensive <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">urban rail</a> network in the UK outside London with rail services travelling to a large part of the <a href="/wiki/Strathclyde" title="Strathclyde">West of Scotland</a>. Most lines were electrified under <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a>. All trains running within Scotland, including the local Glasgow trains, are operated by <a href="/wiki/Abellio_ScotRail" title="Abellio ScotRail">Abellio ScotRail</a>, who own the franchise as determined by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Central station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Queen_Street_railway_station" title="Glasgow Queen Street railway station">Queen Street station</a> are the two main railway terminals. Glasgow Central is the terminus of the 641.6-kilometre (398.7&#160;mi) long <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">London Euston</a>. All services to and from England use this station. Glasgow Central is also the terminus for suburban services on the south side of Glasgow, Ayrshire and Inverclyde, as well as being served by the cross city link from Dalmuir to Motherwell. Most other services within Scotland&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the main line to Edinburgh, plus services to Aberdeen, Dundee, Inverness and the Western Highlands&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 operate from Queen Street station.\n</p><p>The city\'s suburban network is currently divided by the River Clyde, and the <a href="/wiki/Crossrail_Glasgow" title="Crossrail Glasgow">Crossrail Glasgow</a> initiative has been proposed to link them; it is currently awaiting funding from the Scottish Government. The city is linked to Edinburgh by <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_to_Edinburgh_Lines" title="Glasgow to Edinburgh Lines">four direct railway links</a>. In addition to the suburban rail network, SPT operates the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Subway" title="Glasgow Subway">Glasgow Subway</a>. The Subway is the United Kingdom\'s only completely underground <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system, and is generally recognised as the world\'s third underground railway after the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Metro" title="Budapest Metro">Budapest Metro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Both rail and subway stations have a number of <a href="/wiki/Park_and_ride" title="Park and ride">park and ride</a> facilities.\n</p><p>As part of the wider regeneration along the banks of the River Clyde a <a href="/wiki/Bus_Rapid_Transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Bus Rapid Transit">Bus Rapid Transit</a> system called <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Fastlink" title="Clyde Fastlink">Clyde Fastlink</a> is operational between Glasgow City Centre to the Queen Elizabeth University Hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:708px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_station_panoramic.JPG" class="image" title="View of Glasgow Central station (with the distinctive fa\xc3\xa7ade of the Heilanman&#39;s Umbrella to the left) from the 5th floor of Radisson SAS hotel, May 2009"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Central_station_panoramic.JPG/700px-Central_station_panoramic.JPG" width="700" height="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Central_station_panoramic.JPG/1050px-Central_station_panoramic.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Central_station_panoramic.JPG/1400px-Central_station_panoramic.JPG 2x" data-file-width="7251" data-file-height="1766" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_station_panoramic.JPG" title="File:Central station panoramic.JPG"> </a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow Central station</a> (with the distinctive fa\xc3\xa7ade of the <a href="/wiki/Heilanman%27s_Umbrella" class="mw-redirect" title="Heilanman&#39;s Umbrella">Heilanman\'s Umbrella</a> to the left) from the 5th floor of <a href="/wiki/Radisson_SAS" class="mw-redirect" title="Radisson SAS">Radisson SAS</a> hotel, May 2009</div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">Shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Ferries used to link opposite sides of the Clyde in Glasgow but they have been rendered near-obsolete, by bridges and tunnels including the <a href="/wiki/Erskine_Bridge" title="Erskine Bridge">Erskine Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Bridge,_Glasgow" title="Kingston Bridge, Glasgow">Kingston Bridge</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Tunnel" title="Clyde Tunnel">Clyde Tunnel</a>. The only remaining crossings are the <a href="/wiki/Renfrew_Ferry" title="Renfrew Ferry">Renfrew Ferry</a> between <a href="/wiki/Renfrew" title="Renfrew">Renfrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yoker" title="Yoker">Yoker</a>, and the Kilcreggan Ferry in <a href="/wiki/Inverclyde" title="Inverclyde">Inverclyde</a>, both run by SPT but outwith the city boundary. The <i><a href="/wiki/PS_Waverley" title="PS Waverley">PS Waverley</a></i>, the world\'s last operational seagoing <a href="/wiki/Paddle_steamer" title="Paddle steamer">paddle-steamer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> provides services from Glasgow city Centre, mainly catering to the pleasure cruise market. A regular <a href="/wiki/Water_taxi" title="Water taxi">waterbus</a> service links the city Centre with <a href="/wiki/Braehead" title="Braehead">Braehead</a> in Renfrewshire, some 30 minutes downstream. A service by <a href="/wiki/Loch_Lomond_Seaplanes" title="Loch Lomond Seaplanes">Loch Lomond Seaplanes</a>, connecting the city with destinations in <a href="/wiki/Argyll_and_Bute" title="Argyll and Bute">Argyll and Bute</a> started in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The only operational dock left in Glasgow operated by <a href="/wiki/Peel_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Peel Group">Clydeport</a> is the <a href="/wiki/King_George_V_Dock,_Glasgow" title="King George V Dock, Glasgow">King George V Dock</a>, near Braehead. Since the advent of <a href="/wiki/Containerization" title="Containerization">Containerisation</a>, most other facilities, such as <a href="/wiki/Hunterston_Terminal" title="Hunterston Terminal">Hunterston Terminal</a> are located in the deep waters of the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Clyde#Shipping_in_the_Firth" title="Firth of Clyde">Firth of Clyde</a>, which together handle some 7.5&#160;million tonnes of cargo each year. Longer distant commercial sea shipping from Glasgow occurs regularly to many European destinations including Mediterranean and Baltic ports via passage through the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_the_Hebrides" title="Sea of the Hebrides">Sea of the Hebrides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg/220px-Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg/330px-Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg/440px-Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wfm_m8_motorway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/M8_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M8 motorway (Scotland)">M8</a>, Scotland\'s busiest <a href="/wiki/Motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway">motorway</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The main M8 motorway passes through the city centre and connects to the <a href="/wiki/M77_motorway" title="M77 motorway">M77</a>, <a href="/wiki/M73_motorway" title="M73 motorway">M73</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M80_motorway" title="M80 motorway">M80</a> motorways. The <a href="/wiki/A82_road" title="A82 road">A82</a> connects the city to <a href="/wiki/Argyll_and_Bute" title="Argyll and Bute">Argyll</a> and the western <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Highlands</a>. The <a href="/wiki/A74(M)_and_M74_motorways" title="A74(M) and M74 motorways">M74</a> runs directly south towards <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a>; the M74 completion scheme has extended the motorway from Tollcross into the <a href="/wiki/Tradeston" title="Tradeston">Tradeston</a> area to join the M8.\n</p><p>Other road projects in the city include <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_East_End_Regeneration_Route" title="Glasgow East End Regeneration Route">East End Regeneration Route</a>, which aims to provide easier access to deprived areas of the East End by linking the M8 to the extended M74.\n</p><p>The M8 motorway that crosses the River Clyde, crosses on the Kingston Bridge. This is the busiest bridge in Europe.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The city has three international airports within 45 minutes travel of the city centre, as well as a centrally-located seaplane terminal. Two are dedicated to Glasgow while the third is Edinburgh International which, as it is situated on the west side of Edinburgh, is relatively close to Glasgow. These airports are <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow Airport</a> (GLA) (8 miles (10&#160;km) west of the city centre) in Renfrewshire, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Prestwick_Airport" title="Glasgow Prestwick Airport">Glasgow Prestwick Airport</a> (PIK) (30 miles (50&#160;km) south west) in Ayrshire, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh Airport</a> (EDI), (34 miles (50&#160;km) east) in Edinburgh, and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Seaplane_Terminal" title="Glasgow Seaplane Terminal">Glasgow Seaplane Terminal</a>, by the Glasgow Science Centre on the River Clyde. There are also several smaller, domestic and private airports around the city. There is a heliport, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_Heliport" title="Glasgow City Heliport">Glasgow City Heliport</a> located at Stobcross Quay on the banks of the Clyde.\n</p><p>All of the international airports are easily accessibly by public transport, with GLA and EDI directly linked by a bus routes from the main bus station, and a direct rail connection to PIK from Glasgow Central Station. A plan to provide a direct rail link to Glasgow International was dropped with the cancelling of the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a> in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> though the Scottish Government is actively, as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, considering alternative rail-based surface-access possibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Housing_in_Glasgow" title="Housing in Glasgow">Housing in Glasgow</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg/220px-Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg/330px-Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg/440px-Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="517" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dudley_Drive_-_geograph.org.uk_-_580164.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical red sandstone Glasgow tenement in <a href="/wiki/Hyndland" title="Hyndland">Hyndland</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow is known for its <a href="/wiki/Tenements" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenements">tenements</a>; the red and blond <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> buildings are some of the most recognisable features of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> These were the most popular form of housing in 19th- and 20th-century Glasgow, and remain the most common form of dwelling in Glasgow today. Tenements are commonly bought by a wide range of social types and are favoured for their large rooms, high ceilings and original period features.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hyndland" title="Hyndland">Hyndland</a> area of Glasgow is the only tenement conservation area in the UK<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and includes some tenement houses with as many as six bedrooms.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg/250px-AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg/375px-AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg/500px-AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AnderstonCtrMultis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Anderston_Centre" title="Anderston Centre">Blythswood Court</a> estate in <a href="/wiki/Anderston" title="Anderston">Anderston</a>, one of many high-rise schemes in the city constructed in the 1960s and 1970s</div></div></div>\n<p>Like many cities in the UK, Glasgow witnessed the construction of high-rise housing in <a href="/wiki/Tower_block" class="mw-redirect" title="Tower block">tower blocks</a> in the 1960s, along with large <a href="/wiki/Overspill_estate" title="Overspill estate">overspill estates</a> on the periphery of the city, in areas like <a href="/wiki/Pollok" title="Pollok">Pollok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nitshill" title="Nitshill">Nitshill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castlemilk" title="Castlemilk">Castlemilk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Easterhouse" title="Easterhouse">Easterhouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Glasgow" title="Milton, Glasgow">Milton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drumchapel" title="Drumchapel">Drumchapel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> These were built to replace the decaying inner-city tenement buildings originally built for workers who migrated from the surrounding countryside, the Highlands, and the rest of the United Kingdom, particularly Ireland, to feed the local demand for labour.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The massive demand at that time outstripped the pace of new building, and many originally fine tenements often became overcrowded and unsanitary.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Many degenerated into infamous <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a>, such as the Gorbals.\n</p><p>Efforts to improve this housing situation, most successfully with the City Improvement Trust in the late 19th century, cleared the slums of the old town areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Trongate" title="Trongate">Trongate</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_Street_(Glasgow)" class="mw-redirect" title="High Street (Glasgow)">High Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cross" title="Glasgow Cross">Glasgow Cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a> initiatives, such as those motivated by the <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Report" title="Bruce Report">Bruce Report</a>, entailed the comprehensive demolition of slum tenement areas, the development of <a href="/wiki/New_towns_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="New towns in the United Kingdom">new towns</a> on the periphery of the city, and the construction of tower blocks.\n</p><p>The policy of tenement demolition is now considered to have been short-sighted, wasteful and largely unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-Gourlay_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gourlay-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Many of Glasgow\'s worst tenements were refurbished into desirable accommodation in the 1970s and 1980s<sup id="cite_ref-Gourlay_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gourlay-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and the policy of demolition is considered to have destroyed many fine examples of a "universally admired architectural" style.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Housing_Association" title="Glasgow Housing Association">Glasgow Housing Association</a> took ownership of the housing stock from the city council on 7 March 2003, and has begun a \xc2\xa396&#160;million clearance and demolition programme to clear and demolish many of the high-rise flats.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg/200px-Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg" width="200" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg/300px-Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg/400px-Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="471" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Cathedral_and_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_579019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Royal_Infirmary" title="Glasgow Royal Infirmary">Glasgow Royal Infirmary</a> is the city\'s oldest and largest hospital.</div></div></div>\n<p>Medical care is mainly provided by <a href="/wiki/NHS_Scotland" title="NHS Scotland">NHS Scotland</a> and is directly administered by <a href="/wiki/NHS_Greater_Glasgow_and_Clyde" title="NHS Greater Glasgow and Clyde">NHS Greater Glasgow and Clyde</a>.\n</p><p>Major hospitals, including those with <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">Accident &amp; Emergency</a> provision, are: the <a href="/wiki/Western_Infirmary" title="Western Infirmary">Western Infirmary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gartnavel_General_Hospital" title="Gartnavel General Hospital">Gartnavel General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Royal_Infirmary" title="Glasgow Royal Infirmary">Glasgow Royal Infirmary</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Dental_Hospital_and_School" title="Glasgow Dental Hospital and School">Dental Hospital</a> in the city Centre, <a href="/wiki/Stobhill_Hospital" title="Stobhill Hospital">Stobhill Hospital</a> in the North and the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Victoria_Infirmary" title="Glasgow Victoria Infirmary">Victoria Infirmary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_University_Hospital" title="Queen Elizabeth University Hospital">Queen Elizabeth University Hospital</a> in the South Side. <a href="/wiki/Gartnavel_Royal_Hospital" title="Gartnavel Royal Hospital">Gartnavel Royal Hospital</a> and The Priory are the two major psychiatric hospitals based in Glasgow.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_University_Hospital" title="Queen Elizabeth University Hospital">Queen Elizabeth University Hospital</a> (QEUH) Campus is a 1,677-bed acute hospital located in <a href="/wiki/Govan" title="Govan">Govan</a> in the south-west of Glasgow. The hospital is built on the site of the former <a href="/wiki/Southern_General_Hospital" title="Southern General Hospital">Southern General Hospital</a> and opened at the end of April 2015. The hospital comprises a newly built 1,109-bed adult hospital, a 256-bed children\'s hospital and two major A&amp;E departments, one for adults and one for children in addition to buildings retained from the former hospital. The QEUH is the Regional Major Trauma Centre for the west of Scotland<sup id="cite_ref-Healthcare_Improvement_Scotland_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Healthcare_Improvement_Scotland-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and is also the largest hospital campus in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is also an emergency telephone service provided by <a href="/wiki/NHS_24" title="NHS 24">NHS 24</a> and 24-hour access to <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">general practitioners</a> through out of hours centres. <a href="/wiki/Paramedic" title="Paramedic">Paramedic</a> services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Ambulance_Service" title="Scottish Ambulance Service">Scottish Ambulance Service</a> and supported by voluntary bodies like the <a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Ambulance_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Andrew&#39;s Ambulance Association">St. Andrew\'s Ambulance Association</a>. A strong <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching</a> tradition is maintained between the city\'s main hospitals and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow_Medical_School" title="University of Glasgow Medical School">University of Glasgow Medical School</a>.\n</p><p>All pharmacies provide a wide range of services including minor ailment advice, emergency hormonal contraception, public health advice, some provide oxygen and needle exchange.\n</p><p>There are private clinics and hospitals at the <a href="/wiki/Nuffield_Health" title="Nuffield Health">Nuffield</a> in the west end and Ross Hall in the south side of the city.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg/220px-University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg/330px-University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg/440px-University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4056" data-file-height="3099" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Glasgow_Gilbert_Scott_Building_-_Feb_2008-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a> is the fourth oldest university in the English-speaking world and among the world\'s top 100 universities.</div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow is a major centre of higher and academic research, with five universities within 10 miles (16&#160;km) of the city centre:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Strathclyde" title="University of Strathclyde">University of Strathclyde</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Caledonian_University" title="Glasgow Caledonian University">Glasgow Caledonian University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_of_Scotland" title="University of the West of Scotland">University of the West of Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_School_of_Art" title="Glasgow School of Art">The Glasgow School of Art</a><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Saltire_Centre,_GCU.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Saltire_Centre%2C_GCU.jpg/260px-Saltire_Centre%2C_GCU.jpg" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Saltire_Centre%2C_GCU.jpg/390px-Saltire_Centre%2C_GCU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Saltire_Centre%2C_GCU.jpg/520px-Saltire_Centre%2C_GCU.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Saltire_Centre,_GCU.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Saltire Centre at <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Caledonian_University" title="Glasgow Caledonian University">Glasgow Caledonian University</a>, one of the busiest <a href="/wiki/Academic_library" title="Academic library">university libraries</a> in the UK</div></div></div>\n<p>There are also three <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> colleges in the city: <a href="/wiki/City_of_Glasgow_College" title="City of Glasgow College">City of Glasgow College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Clyde_College" title="Glasgow Clyde College">Glasgow Clyde College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Kelvin_College" title="Glasgow Kelvin College">Glasgow Kelvin College</a>. Higher education colleges in the city include <a href="/wiki/Jordanhill_College" title="Jordanhill College">Jordanhill Teacher Training College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Conservatoire_of_Scotland" title="Royal Conservatoire of Scotland">Royal Conservatoire of Scotland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_School_of_Art" title="Glasgow School of Art">Glasgow School of Art</a>.\n</p><p>In 2011 Glasgow had 53,470 full-time students aged 18\xe2\x80\x9374 resident in the city during term time, more than any other city in Scotland and the fifth-largest in the United Kingdom outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The majority of those who live away from home reside in <a href="/wiki/Shawlands" title="Shawlands">Shawlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennistoun" title="Dennistoun">Dennistoun</a> and the West End of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nThe City Council operates 29 secondary schools, 149 primary schools and three specialist schools&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the Dance School of Scotland, <a href="/wiki/Bellahouston_Academy#Glasgow_School_of_Sport" title="Bellahouston Academy">Glasgow School of Sport</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Gaelic_School" title="Glasgow Gaelic School">Glasgow Gaelic School</a> (<i>Sgoil Gh\xc3\xa0idhlig Ghlaschu</i>), the only secondary school in Scotland to teach exclusively in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>. Outdoor Education facilities are provided by the city council at the Blairvadach Centre, near <a href="/wiki/Helensburgh" title="Helensburgh">Helensburgh</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jordanhill_School" title="Jordanhill School">Jordanhill School</a> is operated directly by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>. Glasgow also has a number of <a href="/wiki/Independent_school" title="Independent school">Independent schools</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Hutchesons%27_Grammar_School" title="Hutchesons&#39; Grammar School">Hutchesons\' Grammar School</a> founded in 1639 and one of the oldest school institutions in Britain, and others such as <a href="/wiki/Craigholme_School" title="Craigholme School">Craigholme School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernhill_School" title="Fernhill School">Fernhill School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Academy">Glasgow Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvinside_Academy" title="Kelvinside Academy">Kelvinside Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Aloysius%27_College,_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Aloysius&#39; College, Glasgow">St. Aloysius\' College</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_High_School_of_Glasgow" class="mw-redirect" title="The High School of Glasgow">The High School of Glasgow</a>, which was founded in 1124 and is the oldest school in Scotland.</p><div style="clear:right;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Glasgow" title="Sport in Glasgow">Sport in Glasgow</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Celtic_Park_New.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Celtic_Park_New.jpg/190px-Celtic_Park_New.jpg" width="190" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Celtic_Park_New.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Celtic_Park_New.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Celtic Park</a> in Parkhead is Scotland\'s biggest football stadium.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_football_in_Scotland" title="History of football in Scotland">History of football in Scotland</a></div>\n<p>The world\'s first international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> match was held in 1872 at the <a href="/wiki/West_of_Scotland_Cricket_Club" title="West of Scotland Cricket Club">West of Scotland Cricket Club</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Crescent" title="Hamilton Crescent">Hamilton Crescent</a> ground in the <a href="/wiki/Partick" title="Partick">Partick</a> area of the city. The match, between <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> finished 0\xe2\x80\x930.\n</p><p>Glasgow was the first city (since joined by <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> in 1985, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> in 1986, 2014, 2016 and 2018, and <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> in 1994) to have had two football teams in European finals in the same season:<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> in 1967, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> competed in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> final with rivals <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a> competing in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners&#39; Cup">Cup Winners\' Cup</a> final. Rangers were the first football club from the United Kingdom to reach a European final, doing so in <a href="/wiki/1961_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1961 European Cup Winners&#39; Cup Final">1961</a>. They have also won more domestic top tier league titles than any other football club in the world (currently 54). Celtic were the first non-Latin club to win the European Cup, under the management of <a href="/wiki/Jock_Stein" title="Jock Stein">Jock Stein</a> in <a href="/wiki/1966%E2%80%9367_European_Cup" title="1966\xe2\x80\x9367 European Cup">1967</a>, before <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> the following year. Celtic also went on to reach another European Cup Final in <a href="/wiki/1970_European_Cup_Final" title="1970 European Cup Final">1970</a>, losing to <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</a>, and also the final of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2003_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2003 UEFA Cup Final">2003</a>, where they lost an enthralling match which finished 3\xe2\x80\x932 to Portuguese club <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a>. Rangers also reached the final of the same competition in <a href="/wiki/2008_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2008 UEFA Cup Final">2008</a>, where they lost to <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> of Russia.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a>, which is Scotland\'s national football stadium, holds the European record for attendance at a football match: 149,547<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> saw Scotland beat England 3\xe2\x80\x931 in 1937, in the days before leading British stadia became <a href="/wiki/All-seater_stadium" title="All-seater stadium">all-seated</a>.
