Hampden Park has hosted the final of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> on three occasions, most recently in 2002 and hosted the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> Final in 2007. <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Celtic Park</a> (60,355 seats) is located in the east end of Glasgow, and <a href="/wiki/Ibrox_Stadium" title="Ibrox Stadium">Ibrox Stadium</a> (50,947 seats) on the south side.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg/190px-Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg" width="190" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg/285px-Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg/380px-Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ibrox_and_surrounds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ibrox_Stadium" title="Ibrox Stadium">Ibrox Stadium</a> is Scotland\'s only UEFA Elite stadium.</div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow has three professional football clubs: Celtic, Rangers, and <a href="/wiki/Partick_Thistle_F.C." title="Partick Thistle F.C.">Partick Thistle</a>. A fourth, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queen\'s Park</a>, operate on an amateur basis in the SPFL League 2 and are one of the world\'s oldest active clubs (founded 1867). Prior to this, Glasgow had two other professional teams: <a href="/wiki/Clyde_F.C." title="Clyde F.C.">Clyde</a> (since moved to <a href="/wiki/Cumbernauld" title="Cumbernauld">Cumbernauld</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Third_Lanark_A.C." title="Third Lanark A.C.">Third Lanark</a> (liquidated in 1967), plus four others active in the league in the 19th century: <a href="/wiki/Thistle_F.C." title="Thistle F.C.">Thistle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cowlairs_F.C." title="Cowlairs F.C.">Cowlairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_F.C." title="Northern F.C.">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linthouse_F.C." title="Linthouse F.C.">Linthouse</a>. There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Junior_Football_Association" title="Scottish Junior Football Association">Junior</a> clubs within the city as well, such as <a href="/wiki/Pollok_F.C." title="Pollok F.C.">Pollok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryhill_F.C." title="Maryhill F.C.">Maryhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benburb_F._C." class="mw-redirect" title="Benburb F. C.">Benburb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashfield_F.C." title="Ashfield F.C.">Ashfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Perthshire_F.C." title="Glasgow Perthshire F.C.">Glasgow Perthshire F.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shettleston_F.C." title="Shettleston F.C.">Shettleston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petershill_F.C." title="Petershill F.C.">Petershill</a>, as well as numerous amateur teams.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg/220px-West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg/330px-West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg/440px-West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:West_Stand_Hampden_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queens Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland national football team</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The history of football in the city, as well as the status of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Firm" title="Old Firm">Old Firm</a>, attracts many visitors to football matches in the city throughout the season. The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">Scottish Football Association</a>, the national governing body, and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Museum" title="Scottish Football Museum">Scottish Football Museum</a> are based in Glasgow, as are the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Professional_Football_League" title="Scottish Professional Football League">Scottish Professional Football League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Junior_Football_Association" title="Scottish Junior Football Association">Scottish Junior Football Association</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Amateur_Football_Association" title="Scottish Amateur Football Association">Scottish Amateur Football Association</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Cup" title="Glasgow Cup">Glasgow Cup</a> was a once popular tournament, which was competed for by Rangers, Celtic, Clyde, Partick Thistle and Queen\'s Park. The competition is now played for by the youth sides of the five teams.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JHS@Firhill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/JHS%40Firhill.jpg/220px-JHS%40Firhill.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/JHS%40Firhill.jpg/330px-JHS%40Firhill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/JHS%40Firhill.jpg/440px-JHS%40Firhill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JHS@Firhill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Firhill_Stadium" title="Firhill Stadium">Firhill Stadium</a> is the home of <a href="/wiki/Partick_Thistle_F.C." title="Partick Thistle F.C.">Partick Thistle</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Maryhill" title="Maryhill">Maryhill</a> district of the city.</div></div></div>\n<p>Glasgow is also home to six women\'s football teams. Currently, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_City_F.C." title="Glasgow City F.C.">Glasgow City</a> are the champions of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Women%27s_Premier_League" title="Scottish Women&#39;s Premier League">Scottish Women\'s Premier League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Other local teams include <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Girls_F.C." title="Glasgow Girls F.C.">Glasgow Girls</a> and the women\'s sections of the men\'s clubs: <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C._Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic F.C. Women">Celtic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangers_L.F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Rangers L.F.C.">Rangers</a> play in the top division.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Club\n</th>\n<th>Founded\n</th>\n<th>League\n</th>\n<th>Venue\n</th>\n<th>Capacity\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic F.C.</a>\n</td>\n<td>1888\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premiership" title="Scottish Premiership">Scottish Premiership</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Celtic Park</a>\n</td>\n<td>60,411<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Partick_Thistle_F.C." title="Partick Thistle F.C.">Partick Thistle F.C.</a>\n</td>\n<td>1876\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Championship" title="Scottish Championship">Scottish Championship</a>\n</td>\n<td><a id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queen\'s Park F.C.</a>\n</td>\n<td>1867\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scottish_League_Two" title="Scottish League Two">Scottish League Two</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a>\n</td>\n<td>51,866<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_union">Rugby union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Rugby union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Glasgow has a professional <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> club, the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Warriors" title="Glasgow Warriors">Glasgow Warriors</a>, which plays in the European Rugby Champions Cup and <a href="/wiki/Pro14" title="Pro14">Pro14</a> alongside teams from Scotland, Ireland, Wales and Italy. The Warriors current home is Scotstoun Stadium and has been since 2012, previously they played at Firhill Stadium. They have won the Melrose 7s in both 2014 and 2015 and were also crowned champions of the Pro12 at the end of the 2014/15 season after beating Irish side Munster in Belfast.\n</p><p>In the Scottish League, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Hawks_RFC" title="Glasgow Hawks RFC">Glasgow Hawks RFC</a> was formed in 1997 by the merger of two of Glasgow\'s oldest clubs: Glasgow Academicals and Glasgow High Kelvinside (GHK). Despite the merger, the second division teams of Glasgow Academicals and Glasgow High Kelvinside re-entered the Scottish rugby league in 1998.\n</p><p>In the South Glasgow suburb of Giffnock is based another of Glasgow\'s most prominent clubs <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Hutchesons_Aloysians_RFC" title="Glasgow Hutchesons Aloysians RFC">Glasgow Hutchesons Aloysians RFC</a> (GHA). GHA was formed in 2002 with the merger of two of Glasgow\'s leading clubs at the time, Glasgow Southern RFC and Hutchesons\' Aloysians RFC. Cartha Queen\'s Park play at Dumbreck.\n</p><p>Glasgow is also home to one of the oldest rugby clubs in Scotland,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/West_of_Scotland_F.C." title="West of Scotland F.C.">West of Scotland F.C.</a>, which was formed in 1865, and was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Rugby_Union" title="Scottish Rugby Union">Scottish Rugby Union</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_league">Rugby league</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Rugby league">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Easterhouse_Panthers" title="Easterhouse Panthers">Easterhouse Panthers</a> based in the East End of Glasgow are a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team who play in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Conference_Scotland_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League Conference Scotland Division">Rugby League Conference Scotland Division</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scotstoun_Stadium" title="Scotstoun Stadium">Scotstoun Stadium</a> has also hosted many <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> tournaments/events.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey">Ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The City of Glasgow has a number of ice rinks, and a temporary one is set up in George Square in the Christmas period, however this was not the case in 2016.\n</p><p>From 1966 to 1986, the Glasgow Dynamos played at Crossmyloof Ice Rink.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Since October 2010 a team called the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Clan" title="Glasgow Clan">Glasgow Clan</a> based in the nearby <a href="/wiki/Braehead_Arena" title="Braehead Arena">Braehead Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Renfrewshire" title="Renfrewshire">Renfrewshire</a> has played in the professional <a href="/wiki/Elite_Ice_Hockey_League" title="Elite Ice Hockey League">Elite Ice Hockey League</a> alongside three other Scottish teams, the <a href="/wiki/Fife_Flyers" title="Fife Flyers">Fife Flyers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dundee_Stars" title="Dundee Stars">Dundee Stars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Capitals" title="Edinburgh Capitals">Edinburgh Capitals</a>. This is the first time that a top level <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team has represented Glasgow.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swimming">Swimming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Swimming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arlington_Baths_Club" title="Arlington Baths Club">Arlington Baths Club</a> is the oldest swimming club in the world, founded in 1870. The Club in Arlington Street, in the <a href="/wiki/Woodlands,_Glasgow" title="Woodlands, Glasgow">Woodlands</a> area of the city is still thriving today. It is believed the Club\'s first Baths Master <a href="/wiki/William_Wilson_(aquatics)" title="William Wilson (aquatics)">William Wilson</a> invented <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> at the Club. The Arlington inspired other Swimming Clubs and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Baths" title="Western Baths">Western Baths</a>, which opened in 1876, is also still in existence in nearby <a href="/wiki/Hillhead" title="Hillhead">Hillhead</a>. Most of Glasgow\'s Victorian and Edwardian Municipal Pools have been closed or demolished, with the city council investing in large new leisure centres such as <a href="/wiki/Tollcross_International_Swimming_Centre" title="Tollcross International Swimming Centre">Tollcross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Springburn" title="Springburn">Springburn</a>, Gorbals, <a href="/wiki/Scotstoun" title="Scotstoun">Scotstoun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bellahouston" title="Bellahouston">Bellahouston</a>. A community group is however hoping to re-open <a href="/wiki/Govanhill" title="Govanhill">Govanhill</a> Baths, on the city\'s southside.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Glasgow hosts Scotland\'s only professional basketball team, the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Rocks" title="Glasgow Rocks">Glasgow Rocks</a>, who compete in the <a href="/wiki/British_Basketball_League" title="British Basketball League">British Basketball League</a>. Previously based in Renfrewshire\'s <a href="/wiki/Braehead_Arena" title="Braehead Arena">Braehead Arena</a> and the 1,200 seater Kelvin Hall, the team has been based at the Emirates Arena since the 2012/13 season.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Arena_(geograph_4624258).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Emirates_Arena_%28geograph_4624258%29.jpg/220px-Emirates_Arena_%28geograph_4624258%29.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Emirates_Arena_%28geograph_4624258%29.jpg/330px-Emirates_Arena_%28geograph_4624258%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Emirates_Arena_%28geograph_4624258%29.jpg/440px-Emirates_Arena_%28geograph_4624258%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="338" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Arena_(geograph_4624258).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Emirates_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Emirates Arena">Emirates Arena</a> in Glasgow, one of the designated stadiums constructed for the 2014 Commonwealth Games</div></div></div>\n<p>Major international sporting arenas include the Kelvin Hall and <a href="/wiki/Scotstoun" title="Scotstoun">Scotstoun</a> Sports Centre. In 2003 the National Academy for Badminton was completed in Scotstoun. In 2003, Glasgow was also given the title of <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="European Capital of Sport">European Capital of Sport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Glasgow is also host to many <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> clubs including <a href="/wiki/Clydesdale_Cricket_Club" title="Clydesdale Cricket Club">Clydesdale Cricket Club</a> who have been title winners for the Scottish Cup many times. This club also acted as a neutral venue for a <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> match between <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_national_cricket_team" title="Pakistan national cricket team">Pakistan</a> in 2007, but due to bad weather it was called off.\n</p><p>Smaller sporting facilities include an abundance of outdoor <a href="/wiki/Playing_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Playing field">playing fields</a>, as well as golf clubs such as <a href="/wiki/Haggs_Castle" title="Haggs Castle">Haggs Castle</a> and artificial ski slopes. Between 1998 and 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Claymores" title="Scottish Claymores">Scottish Claymores</a> <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team played some or all of their home games each season at Hampden Park and the venue also hosted <a href="/wiki/World_Bowl" title="World Bowl">World Bowl</a> XI.\n</p><p>Glasgow Green and the <a href="/wiki/Gorbals" title="Gorbals">Gorbals</a> are home to a number of <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a> clubs, some with open membership the rest belonging to universities or schools. Historically, rowing races on the <a href="/wiki/River_Clyde" title="River Clyde">River Clyde</a> here attracted huge crowds of spectators to watch regattas in the late 19th century and early 20th century;<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> before football caught the public imagination. Two of Glasgow\'s rowing clubs separately claim that it was their members who were among the founders of Rangers Football Club.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">Motorcycle speedway</a> racing was first introduced to Glasgow in 1928 and is currently staged at Saracen Park in the North of the city. The home club, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Tigers_(speedway)" title="Glasgow Tigers (speedway)">Glasgow Tigers</a>, compete in the British Premier League, the second tier of motorcycle speedway in Britain.\n</p><p>Glasgow is also one of five places in Scotland that hosts the final of the Scottish Cup of <a href="/wiki/Shinty" title="Shinty">Shinty</a>, better known as the <a href="/wiki/Camanachd_Cup" title="Camanachd Cup">Camanachd Cup</a>. This is usually held at Old Anniesland. Once home to numerous Shinty clubs, there is now only one senior club in Glasgow, Glasgow Mid-Argyll, as well as two university sides from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strathclyde" title="University of Strathclyde">University of Strathclyde</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>.\n</p><p>Glasgow <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_bid_for_the_2018_Summer_Youth_Olympics" title="Glasgow bid for the 2018 Summer Youth Olympics">bid</a> to host the <a href="/wiki/2018_Summer_Youth_Olympics" title="2018 Summer Youth Olympics">2018 Summer Youth Olympics</a> but lost to <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> in 4 July 2013 vote.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Glasgow will host the <a href="/wiki/2018_European_Sports_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="2018 European Sports Championships">2018</a> <a href="/wiki/European_Sports_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="European Sports Championships">European Sports Championships</a> along with Berlin (pre-existing hosts of the <a href="/wiki/2018_European_Athletics_Championships" title="2018 European Athletics Championships">2018 European Athletics Championships</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Commonwealth_Games">2014 Commonwealth Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: 2014 Commonwealth Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="2014 Commonwealth Games">2014 Commonwealth Games</a></div>\n<p>On 9 November 2007, Glasgow was selected to be the host city of the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>. The games were held at a number of existing and newly constructed sporting venues across the city, including a refurbished <a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvingrove_Park" title="Kelvingrove Park">Kelvingrove Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelvin_Hall" title="Kelvin Hall">Kelvin Hall</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/SSE_Hydro" title="SSE Hydro">SSE Hydro</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Exhibition_and_Conference_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Exhibition and Conference Centre">SECC</a>. The opening ceremony was held at Celtic Park. 2014 was the third time the Games have been held in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RobertMcAlpine_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RobertMcAlpine-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_incidents_and_tragedies">Major incidents and tragedies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Major incidents and tragedies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>5 April 1902 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/1902_Ibrox_disaster" title="1902 Ibrox disaster">1902 Ibrox disaster</a> \xe2\x80\x93 25 spectators died and 500 were injured when a new wooden stand at the stadium collapsed.</li>\n<li>1960s/1970s \xe2\x80\x93 several firefighters perished at three separate blazes: the <a href="/wiki/Cheapside_Street_whisky_bond_fire" title="Cheapside Street whisky bond fire">Cheapside Street whisky bond fire</a> (1960, 19 killed); the <a href="/wiki/James_Watt_Street_fire" title="James Watt Street fire">James Watt Street fire</a> (1968, 22 killed); the <a href="/wiki/Kilbirnie_Street_fire" title="Kilbirnie Street fire">Kilbirnie Street fire</a> (1972, seven killed).</li>\n<li>2 January 1971 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/1971_Ibrox_disaster" title="1971 Ibrox disaster">1971 Ibrox disaster</a> \xe2\x80\x93 66 people were killed in a crush, as supporters attempted to vacate the stadium.</li>\n<li>11 May 2004 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Stockline_Plastics_factory_explosion" title="Stockline Plastics factory explosion">Stockline Plastics factory explosion</a> \xe2\x80\x93 The ICL Plastics factory (commonly referred to as Stockline Plastics factory), in the Woodside district of Glasgow in western Scotland, exploded. Nine people were killed, including two company directors, and 33 injured \xe2\x80\x93 15 seriously. The four-storey building was largely destroyed.</li>\n<li>30 June 2007 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/2007_Glasgow_International_Airport_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Glasgow International Airport attack">Glasgow Airport Terrorist Attack</a> \xe2\x80\x93 On Saturday 30 June 2007 at 15:11BST a Green Jeep Cherokee loaded with propane canisters was driven into the glass doors of the Glasgow International Airport terminal and set ablaze. It was the first terrorist attack in Scotland since the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Lockerbie Bombing</a> in 1988. Security Bollards outside prevented the car from entering the terminal. The car\'s occupants were severely burnt in the ensuing fire and five members of the public suffered minor injuries, some from assisting Police Constables in arresting the occupants. One occupant later died of his injuries in hospital and the second was convicted of attempted murder through terrorism and interfering with International Aerospace and was sentenced to 32 years in custody. A further eight were arrested in connection with the incident, all remanded in custody.</li>\n<li>29 November 2013 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/2013_Glasgow_helicopter_crash" title="2013 Glasgow helicopter crash">2013 Glasgow helicopter crash</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Friday, 29 November 2013 a Eurocopter EC135-T2+ operated by Bond Air Services for Police Scotland fell from the sky and crashed on top of the Clutha Vaults, a pub on the north banks of the River Clyde. Ten people were killed in the incident: all those on the Helicopter, and seven on the ground and inside the pub. The reason why the helicopter crashed is still under investigation.</li>\n<li>23 May 2014 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_School_of_Art#2014_fire" title="Glasgow School of Art">Glasgow School of Art blaze</a> \xe2\x80\x93 A fire tore through the historic and world-renowned Glasgow School of Art Mackintosh building, that was designed by Charles Rennie Mackintosh. Around a tenth of the structure and 30% of its contents were destroyed, including the prized Mackintosh Library. There were no deaths but a few were treated for minor smoke inhalation. The Scottish Fire and Rescue were praised for their quick response and plan to effectively tackle the fire. It was later found after a fire investigation that gases inside a projector had overheated and ignited.</li>\n<li>22 December 2014 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/2014_Glasgow_bin_lorry_crash" title="2014 Glasgow bin lorry crash">2014 Glasgow bin lorry crash</a> \xe2\x80\x93 At about 14:30 GMT, six people were killed and many were seriously injured when a bin lorry careered out of control and collided with pedestrians and a Skoda Octavia Private Hire car before it stopped outside the Millennium Hotel. It is believed that the lorry driver suffered from heart difficulties but the exact cause is still under investigation.</li>\n<li>29 December 2014 \xe2\x80\x93 first <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus" title="Ebola virus">Ebola virus</a> case in Scotland \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Cafferkey" title="Pauline Cafferkey">Pauline Cafferkey</a>, a nurse returning to Glasgow from <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Town" title="Kerry Town">Kerry Town</a> treatment centre, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> where she had been a volunteer caring for patients infected with the Ebola virus was taken into isolation after testing positive for the virus. She was not diagnosed before leaving Sierra Leone.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
